## Thread: Single Source CICS/Batch — 2 this month / 13 total

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Single Source CICS/Batch

- **From:** "Charles Hottel" <chottel@earthlink.net>
- **Date:** 2006-11-01T00:27:42+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<2SR1h.489$0r.112@newsread1.news.pas.earthlink.net>`

#### ↳ Re: Single Source CICS/Batch

- **From:** "Charles Hottel" <chottel@earthlink.net>
- **Date:** 2006-11-02T00:53:18+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<2kb2h.924$ig4.353@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net>`
- **References:** `<H2I0h.153095$qQ7.2376813@phobos.telenet-ops.be>`

```

"Vanroy - Cleymans" <vanroy@pandora.be> wrote in message 
news:H2I0h.153095$qQ7.2376813@phobos.telenet-ops.be...
> Does anybody has experience with writung the Cobol source code once and
> running the load module(s) in Cics and Batch environment (on Z/OS)
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>

I have not done this myself, but I found one example.  Again I did not code 
this and I have not had time to give much thought to how I would code it.

Here is an overview before I give the code. Subroutine AA240901 is the 
subroutine to be executed from both batch and CICS.

The batch part is as usual. Program AIUT06 calls AA240901 using a static 
call.

From CICS, program CQAMSL issues a dynamic CALL to a CICS program, CPP153, 
that is an interface to the AA240901 subroutine. Note that AA240901 has no 
EXEC CICS commands. I think a dynamic call was used because it is faster 
than a EXEC CICS LINK. The interface program, CPP153 does a static CALL to 
the subprogram.

Here is the code:

First the batch caller AIUT06:

        IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
        PROGRAM-ID. AIUT06.
            .
            . This just a regular static batch call
            .
        PROCEDURE DIVISION.
            ENTRY 'DBMSCBL'.
       *---------------------------------------------------------------*
       *    MAIN CONTROL PARAGRAPH OF AIUT0601                       * *
       *---------------------------------------------------------------*
        1000-MAIN-CONTROL.

            MOVE CALENDAR-TO-JULIAN   TO   DR-CMD.
            ACCEPT WS-CURR-DATE       FROM DATE.

            MOVE WS-CURR-YY           TO   YY OF DR-DATE.
            MOVE WS-CURR-MM           TO   MM OF DR-DATE.
            MOVE WS-CURR-DD           TO   DD OF DR-DATE.

            CALL 'AA240901' USING DATE-REQUEST-AREA.

            IF DR-ERROR
               DISPLAY 'DATE ROUTINE ERROR FOR CUR DATE:' DR-RET-CODE
            ELSE
               MOVE        YY OF DR-DATE TO   CURR-PROCESS-YEAR
               MOVE           DR-JUL-DAY TO   CURR-PROCESS-DAY
 Y2KJ01        IF CURR-PROCESS-YEAR > 39
 Y2KJ01            MOVE 19               TO   CURR-PROCESS-CENTURY
 Y2KJ01        ELSE
 Y2KJ01            MOVE 20               TO   CURR-PROCESS-CENTURY
 Y2KJ01        END-IF
            END-IF.
            .
            .
            .

***********************************************************************

Now the CICS caller CQAMSL:

        ID DIVISION.
        PROGRAM-ID.     CQAMSL.
            .
            .  This is a regular CICS program making a dynamic call to the
            .  interface routine, CPP153, which then calls the date routine
            .  AA240901. The call to the date routine is a static call.
            .
            05  WS-C-DATE-ROUTINE       PIC X(08)  VALUE 'CPP153'.
            05  WS-COMMAREA-BYTE        PIC X(01)  VALUE SPACES.
            .
            .
            .
        BUILD-ALL-WINDOWS.

            MOVE SPACES                   TO DATE-REQUEST-AREA.

            SET DR-CALENDAR-TO-JULIAN     TO TRUE.
            MOVE WS-AWB-SPLIT-REC(44:8)   TO DR-CCYYMMDD.

            CALL WS-C-DATE-ROUTINE     USING DFHEIBLK
                                             WS-COMMAREA-BYTE
                                             DATE-REQUEST-AREA.
            IF  DR-ERROR
                MOVE 'BAD RETURN FROM DATE ROUTINE'
                                         TO ACS-ERR-TEXT1
                MOVE DR-RET-CODE         TO ACS-ERR-TEXT2
                SET ACS-ERR-SEV-CRITICAL
                    ACS-ERR-TYPE-OTHER   TO TRUE
                GO TO Z9999-EXIT
            END-IF.

            MOVE DR-JULIAN-DATE-N        TO WS-HOLD-JULIAN-DATE.
            .
            .
            .
***********************************************************************

Now the CICS interface program CPP153:

        ID DIVISION.
        PROGRAM-ID. CPP153.
        AUTHOR. XXX.
        DATE-COMPILED.
       ***************************************************************
       **                   MODIFICATION LOG                        **
       **                                                           **
       **                VERSION 01 - 12 AUG 97                     **
       **                        CPP153                             **
       ***************************************************************
 B04   ** CXXXX   03/08/00   XXXXXXXXX                              **
 B04   **       PROGRAM WAS MODIFIED TO ALLOW IT TO BE LINKED OR    **
 B04   **       DYNAMICALLY CALLED.                                 **
       ***************************************************************
       *    THIS MODULE SERVES AS THE INTERFACE BETWEEN CICS AND     *
       *    MODULE AA2409  WHICH IS A BATCH SUBROUTINE TO CONVERT    *
       *    THE FORMAT OF A DATE.                                    *
       ***************************************************************
        ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.

        DATA DIVISION.
        WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
        77  FILLER                  PIC X(32) VALUE
                'WORKING STORAGE BEGINS HERE'.
 B04    77  WS-ORIGINAL-EIBFN        PIC X(2) VALUE LOW-VALUES.
 B04    77  WS-ORIGINAL-EIBRSRCE     PIC X(8) VALUE LOW-VALUES.
 B04    77  WS-LINK-EIBFN-LIT        PIC S9(04) COMP VALUE +3586.
 B04    77  WS-LINK-EIBFN REDEFINES
 B04          WS-LINK-EIBFN-LIT      PIC X(2).
 B04    77  WS-PUSH-EIBFN-LIT        PIC S9(04) COMP VALUE +524.
 B04    77  WS-PUSH-EIBFN REDEFINES
 B04          WS-PUSH-EIBFN-LIT      PIC X(2).

        01  CORE-MARK.
            03  THIS-PGM                PIC X(6) VALUE 'CPP153'.
            03  THIS-PGM-VERSION        PIC X(2) VALUE '04'.

        LINKAGE SECTION.
 B04    01  DFHCOMMAREA.
 B04        05 FILLER             PIC X(1).
       ******************************************************************
       **      PARMLIST FOR SUBROUTINE AA2409 (Y2K DATE ROUTINE)       **
       ******************************************************************
       ******************************************************************
       **             P R O G R A M M I N G    N O T E S               **
       **                                                              **
       **  1.  BEFORE POPULATING FIELDS IN THE PARMLIST, THE CALLING   **
       **      PROGRAM SHOULD MOVE SPACES TO THE DATE-REQUEST-AREA     **
       **                                                              **
       **  2.  AA2409 WILL CONVERT BOTH 6-DIGIT AND 8-DIGIT CALENDAR   **
       **      DATES AS WELL AS 5-DIGIT AND 7-DIGIT JULIAN DATES.      **
       **      IF THERE ARE SPACES IN THE RESPECTIVE CC FIELDS, AA2409 **
       **      WILL ASSUME THAT IT IS DEALING WITH 6-DIGIT CALENDAR OR **
       **      5-DIGIT JULIAN DATES.                                   **
       **                                                              **
       **  3.  AA2409 WILL RETURN TO THE CALLING PROGRAM A FULLY       **
       **      POPULATED PARMLIST NO MATTER WHICH COMMAND IS SPECIFIED.**
       **                                                              **
       **      FOR EXAMPLE:  TO GET THE JULIAN DATE AND THE BINARY     **
       **                    DATE FOR A PARTICULAR CALENDAR DATE, THE  **
       **                    CALLING PROGRAM WILL MOVE THE CALENDAR    **
       **                    DATE TO THE ADR-8-DIGIT-DATE OR           **
       **                    ADR-YYMMDD (IF 6-DIGIT).  AA2409 WILL     **
       **                    RETURN ALL PARMLIST FIELDS POPULATED. A   **
       **                    SECOND CALL IS NOT NECESSARY.             **
       **                                                              **
       **                                                              **
       ******************************************************************
        01  DATE-REQUEST-AREA.
            03  DR-CMD                      PIC X(03).
                88  DR-CALENDAR-TO-JULIAN     VALUE 'CTJ'.
                88  DR-JULIAN-TO-CALENDAR     VALUE 'JTC'.
                88  DR-LOAD-DAY-OF-WEEK       VALUE 'DW '.
                88  DR-LOAD-MONTH-NAME        VALUE 'LMN'.
                88  DR-BINARY-TO-CALENDAR     VALUE 'BTC'.
                88  DR-BINARY-TO-JULIAN       VALUE 'BTJ'.
            03  DR-DATE-N                   PIC 9(08).
            03  DR-8-DIGIT-DATE REDEFINES DR-DATE-N.
                05  DR-CCYYMMDD.
                    07  DR-CENTURY          PIC 9(02).
                    07  DR-YY               PIC 9(02).
                    07  DR-MM               PIC 9(02).
                    07  DR-DD               PIC 9(02).
            03  FILLER REDEFINES DR-DATE-N.
                05  FILLER                  PIC X(02).
                05  DR-YYMMDD               PIC 9(06).
                05  DR-DATE REDEFINES DR-YYMMDD.
                    07  YY                  PIC X(02).
                    07  MM                  PIC X(02).
                    07  DD                  PIC X(02).
                05  DR-6-DIGIT-DATE REDEFINES DR-YYMMDD
                                            PIC 9(06).
            03  DR-JULIAN-DATE-N            PIC 9(07).
            03  DR-7-DIGIT-JULIAN REDEFINES DR-JULIAN-DATE-N.
                05  DR-JULIAN-CCYY          PIC 9(04).
                05  DR-JUL-DAY              PIC 9(03).
            03  FILLER REDEFINES DR-JULIAN-DATE-N.
                05  DR-JULIAN-CC            PIC X(02).
                05  DR-JULIAN-YYDDD         PIC 9(05).
                05  DR-5-DIGIT-JULIAN REDEFINES DR-JULIAN-YYDDD
                                            PIC 9(05).
            03  DR-BIN-DATE                 PIC S9(09) BINARY.
            03  DR-DAY-O-WEEK               PIC S9(09) BINARY.
                88  DAY-IS-SUNDAY             VALUE 1.
                88  DAY-IS-SATURDAY           VALUE 7.
            03  DR-MONTH-NAME               PIC X(04).
            03  DR-QUARTER                  PIC 9(01).
            03  DR-QTR-END                  PIC X(01).
            03  DR-RET-CODE                 PIC X(02).
                88  DR-ERROR                  VALUE '01' THRU '09'.

        01  DATE-REQUEST-COMMANDS.
            03  CALENDAR-TO-JULIAN          PIC X(03)  VALUE 'CTJ'.
            03  JULIAN-TO-CALENDAR          PIC X(03)  VALUE 'JTC'.
            03  LOAD-DAY-OF-WEEK            PIC X(03)  VALUE 'DW '.
            03  LOAD-MONTH-NAME             PIC X(03)  VALUE 'LMN'.
            03  BINARY-TO-CALENDAR          PIC X(03)  VALUE 'BTC'.
            03  BINARY-TO-JULIAN            PIC X(03)  VALUE 'BTJ'.

 B04    PROCEDURE DIVISION USING  DFHEIBLK
 B04                              DFHCOMMAREA
 B04                              DATE-REQUEST-AREA.

 B04        MOVE EIBFN              TO WS-ORIGINAL-EIBFN.
            MOVE EIBRSRCE           TO WS-ORIGINAL-EIBRSRCE.
 B04        IF WS-ORIGINAL-EIBFN          = WS-LINK-EIBFN   AND
               WS-ORIGINAL-EIBRSRCE(1:6) = THIS-PGM
 B04           SET ADDRESS OF DATE-REQUEST-AREA TO
 B04               ADDRESS OF DFHCOMMAREA
            ELSE
               MOVE SPACES          TO WS-ORIGINAL-EIBFN
 B04        END-IF.

        CC100-CALL-BATCH-VERSION.
 B04        CALL 'AA240901' USING DATE-REQUEST-AREA.

 B04        IF WS-ORIGINAL-EIBFN = WS-LINK-EIBFN
 B04           EXEC CICS
 B04                RETURN
 B04           END-EXEC
 B04        END-IF.

        CC999-GOBACK.
            GOBACK.

******************************************************************
Sorry I forgot to download the subroutine but you probably do not need that. 
Let me knoe though if you do and I can get it.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Development and offshoring was Re: IBM file status 97 (was: Prodcuing an output file onlyonFriday?

_(thread depth: 21)_

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2006-11-01T14:26:52+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<eiaarc$s2v$1@reader2.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<1145991557.147344.25680@i40g2000cwc.googlegroups.com> <4qqcmdFohk29U2@individual.net> <ei9t49$cu4$1@reader2.panix.com> <4qrdg3Fo7s52U1@individual.net>`

```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Development and offshoring was Re: IBM file status 97 (was: Prodcuing an output file onlyonFriday?

_(thread depth: 17)_

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2006-11-01T14:25:10+13:00

```
Some responses below...

"Clark Morris" <cfmtech@istar.ca> wrote in message
news:dunuj2lsrlmfl2562ajued527airpmi4db@4ax.com...
> This is in response to a thread of a few months back and my comments
> are interspersed.
…[44 more quoted lines elided]…
> I believe that organizations get the IT they manage for.

That's like saying that in a Democracy, we get the politicians we deserve...
:-) (I agree this is arguable, but having just returned from a couple of
weeks in the United States, I can't believe ANYONE deserves the current
administration... :-))

Sorry, coming back to your point...

Unfortunately that is not always the case. The cost of  in house IT often
balloons... This is usually caused by unforeseen problems, hidden costs,
escalation of costs, and undercalling by accountants who have no real idea
of what is involved. When financial alarms start going off, the usual
response is to stop work. (God forbid the budget should be exceeded and the
Management Team all lose their bonuses...:-))

In good years when the company is making easy profits, this can be accepted,
and the projects will be completed with an increased IT budget, but if
profits fall for any reason the IT budget may stand out like a throbbing
thumb.

Suddenly the question is asked: "If we are a [whatever] Company, why are we
spending [large percentage] of our profit line on things like IT?"  The
option to simply outsource or lease the service, or replace it with a
standard package and do some Business Re-engineering to meet the package
requirements, becomes very attractive.

(Note that the only people likely to object to any of these options are the
IT people; the rest of the business just want a timely solution... Besides,
it is not THEIR jobs that will be axed...)

Here's an interesting exercise...

Find out what the annual IT budget is in the company you work for. Then work
out how much product or service your company must move or sell in order to
cover that budget.

If it is more than 10% of the annual sales, polish up your CV...:-)

I was working many years ago for a photocopying company in Germany. They had
had many years of easy profits with their 'salesmen' really just 'order
takers'. Then it changed. In one year, they went from substantial profit to
a hefty loss. The IT staff, like the rest of the work force, were fairly
blase...this was Germany, there were unions, no jobs were in danger, it was
just a glitch, next year they would be back in profit...

I worked out that to cover the IT budget they would need to make around
50,000,000 photocopies. I had no idea how many they actually did make, but,
given the population of Germany at that time was around 60 million, that
seemed like a pretty big stack of paper.

Sure enough, within 3 months they had brought in a new CEO and the first
thing he did was slash and burn IT. Hundreds of people lost their jobs (self
included; but, being a contractor, I was pretty philosophical about it and I
had already started looking when I did the calculation outlined above...I
was actually out of work for about 10 days...others weren't so lucky).

The point is that even if a Management Team plan their IT, budget for it
carefully, there is no guarantee it will fulfill what is expected of it.
Technology changes so rapidly, ownership of this years cutting edge may find
ou with a heap of obsolescence before the equipment has even been
amortised...



> As computers
> become more powerful, the inefficiencies of packages using external
> tables and mechanisms other than customized code to control processing
> becomes less of a problem.

From the Management point of view, that is the least of the problems anyway.


10,000 thousand cycles measured in
> nanoseconds per cycle with overlapped processing is a lot less of a
> concern than the same number of cycles where the cycles are measured
> in microseconds with no overlap.  The move to outsourcing IT however
> is more questionable.  The computer systems encode and implement the
> organizational practices.

And most of these have 'evolved' over time. Very rarely have the Enterprise
processes been DESIGNED as an integrated whole, from the ground up. They are
bloated, inefficient, and we would love to start over, but nobody dares to,
because it would have unquantifiable risks... Outsourcing or implementing a
package may be a good opportunity to review existing processes and
practices.


> While program coding by what ever method
> (COBOL coding sheets with punched cards, drop down menus and the
> latest shining IDE in Delphi, .NET, etc.) may not be the core
> competence or need of the organization, controlling the way the
> organization works definitely better be.

Definitely!  But that is not an IT function; it is a joint responsibility of
a Managent Team, with IT providing input to it and making sure that what is
being proposed is technically feasible. The methodology and technology
utilised should not have any bearing on it; it is clarifying WHAT is to be
done, not HOW, that is important.

>  If the IT department is
> viewed as unresponsive, that may say more about the communications and
> outsourcing may only exacerbate the problem.

Well, it MAY say more about communication, but in my extensive experience it
doesn't... It is unresponsive because for decades it has been trapped behind
methodologies and 'practise's that simply don't deliver.

Consider the normal approach...

1. Requirements gathering.

A Business Analyst goes and finds out what is needed. How? By talking (and,
hopefully, listening...)  to people on the shop floor. The business people
have traditionally had no idea what computers are capable of (fortunately,
computer literacy is rising exponentially in the general population, but
this is another factor leading to the demise of in-house IT), and the
Analyst has only general ideas about how the Busness functions (but may well
have a programming background, so sees everything in terms of files and
records). It is like a Quantum Physicist talking to a Mechanical Engineer,
about scheduling oil changes on a moped.

Wouldn't it be much better if the Engineers could simply schedule and apply
oil changes without needing to talk to a Physicist?

If oilcans weren't so complex, they could...

2. Functional design.

Analyst translates what was discussed, into the outline of a system.

3. Point 2 above is decomposed into a set of technical specs and it is
signed off. Programming starts.

etc ad nauseum...

We already have three opportunities for poor or misunderstood communication;
programming, testing, debugging will provide more.

Finally, 9 months later, IT triumphantly roll out the new schedule and the
new oilcans and get the Engineers trained on them.

Engineers greet the IT delivery with polite acceptance. The oil points on
the moped have changed and the moped itself has been upgraded. There is a
new motorcycle that has had to be bought to cope with increased deliveries,
and it requires a different schedule. Too much hassle in getting signed off
requirements changed to tell IT about it, so just learn how to use the new
oilcans and do the best we can...

2 months later the new motorcycle seizes and cannot be used; diagnosed as
incorrect oiling.

The Waterfall delivers something like what was required 9 months ago, to a
Business that has moved on and needs support today. IT can NEVER catch up.
Although this is not their fault, they are perceived by the organization as
'failing to deliver'.  (Human Beings are not always fair and reasonable when
assigning blame...)

Now contrast this with outsourcing...

The outsourcer has a vested interest in delivering the goods and keeping the
customer happy. If there are changes they must be managed, but they will be
accommodated if feasible. The customer will be offered the options of havng
the new changes, but the date slipping, or accepting what was agreed, with
release 2 scheduled as quickly as possible behind it, or, for an additional
pament, having the changes incorporated into the current delivery. The
outsourcer's costs are lower; there is no problem with getting added
resource to do the changes the customer has requested. The rate may be
re-negotiated but everyone will be happy.

... or with a package...

The package does what it does. If changes are required the first thing will
be to see why the base system is being deviated from. Tailoring will only be
indertaken when the business case shows it must be and when internal process
re-engineering will not achieve the advantage that tailoring would.

As the package vendor is not part of the company, they can be litigated
against if there is failure to deliver.


> Now changes are visibly
> billable.

Yes, see above.

>With outsourcing the people in IT definitely have a loyalty
> to the provider and are a part of the provider's culture.  Crossing
> country boundaries can exacerbate the communication problem even if
> the countries are the United States and Canada.  Each level of removal
> complicates the legal situation.

But you have a choice; there are many outsourcers, all vying for your
business.

>>2. More and more corporates are seeing the "IT department" as having
>>little
…[31 more quoted lines elided]…
> that the official application would.

I can't believe you wrote that :-) Some 'official applications' I have seen
(and had to 'fix') were far worse than anything an IT illiterate user could
come up with.

However, I cede your point; for the most part, professionally developed and
designed stuff is better than stuff that someone built by reading the Help
files on Access or Excel. (At least, they SHOULD be... :-))

More importantly, if the shaky 'locally-assembled-by-idiots' application is
available TODAY and does everything the user department wants (even if it
doesn't comply with IT 'best practise' and doesn't have logs and controls
and interfaces), but the 'official application' is still 3 months away
because some problems were encountered with downstream feeds or data
migration from an old validation database, or there has just been an OS
upgrade on the mainframe and we have three weeks of regression testing every
existing application, so development has dropped to a very low priority...
then, would you be prepared to tell them they can't use their home made
tool? (I wouldn't...)


> Little details like error
> handling, making sure the inputs are correct, making sure that
> organization policy about items is taken into account, etc. get in the
> way.

No, they CAN get in the way. I have seen local systems that took all of
these factors (and more) into account. A contract I recently completed in
the UK had more Computing Science graduates in the Business than in the IT
department. Some of their 'local systems' were excellent. The world is
changing. There is a rising generation of computer savvy youngsters coming
into business and they don't necessarily want to work in IT. Eventually IT
departments (in the companies that still retain them - many will simply
outsource their network management, help desk, and hardware rollout) will
need to embrace these local systems and ensure that shared resources are
available for local development.

>If the IT department is doing as bad a job as the department
> creating the spreadsheet, then there is no greater problem.  Many
> times IT has to be the mediator between/among departments.  Just
> because something looks right doesn't mean it is right.

Er... I think it usually does... otherwise it would look wrong. :-)

>  Bluntly
> people in the business don't necessarily know exactly what they need
> and these scattered applications may have a good effect on the bottom
> line or a disastrous one.

I'm not advocating duplicated data and 'scattered applications'. I'm
advocating IT working with users and ensuring there are shared resources
available so that local systems can be developed by individual departments
in a way that benefits the oprganisation as a whole. Yes, there are petty
rivalries and jealousies between departments and some of them don't want
certain figures to be publicly available. That has to be addressed, and IT
is a perfect mediator for it. The corporate needs are above the need of any
individual department, but that does't mean that departments can't develop
their own tools and databases.

It has certainly been true that people in the Business haven't always known
what they needed IN IT TERMS. That is changing.

And it is also true that IT specialists don't necessarily know what the
Business needs either...


> This is especially true in an era of PIPEDA
> (privacy act in Canada), Sarbanes Oxley accounting system requirements
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> that he can safely sign certification documents.

This is totally dependent on the individual organisation. How would the CEO
know that an IT developed core system can be relied on?

It isn't about who developed what, it is about the checks and balances that
are in place for ALL systems.

>>
>>3. For the reasons outlined above, the days of the "COBOL shop" (read, "IT
…[79 more quoted lines elided]…
>>
```

"some" <s@mailinator.com> wrote in message 
news:1162400311.788159.253160@i42g2000cwa.googlegroups.com...
> Hi All,

…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Here's my two cents.

There's basic COBOL. COBOL was the first high-level language (developed by a 
committee funded by the Department of Defense) and has been around, like, 
forever. It's not hard to get a grip on the fundamentals like adding, 
reading a file, putting something on the screen or a piece of paper.

Getting COBOL to interact with something outside its own universe - such as 
Windows or SQL - involves much more. Sometimes much MUCH more. With the 
attendant increase in knowledge and expense.

So, get Thane's book (along with the free, basic COBOL compiler) and become 
familiar with the fundamentals of the language. Then you'll have enough 
information to decide if you want to get down in the weeds with the more 
advanced stuff. If you do decide to move forward, perhaps your prospective 
employer will spring for the $2-3,000 for a conforming compiler. Another 
possibility is to intern at a shop that has the tools you need. Do a little 
work (for free), pick up some skills.

The biggest difference between C (or C++ or C#) and COBOL is that it is much 
more difficult to fuck something up big time in COBOL. Oh, it's possible, 
but you really have to work at it. Y2K problems being the obvious exception. 
That is, a catastrophe in C is easy, it's HARD in COBOL (I'm talking buffer 
overflows, pointers going berserk, etc.). Heck, some of my best code was 
done when I was drunk.
```

> There's basic COBOL. COBOL was the first high-level language

It is not even close to being "the first high-level language" and was
predated by many, many, such as Fortran, Algol and Autocode.

In fact Cobol was based on several prior languages such as FlowMatic

In article <12kik1ef4uk4fa2@news.supernews.com>,
HeyBub <heybubNOSPAM@gmail.com> wrote:

[snip]

>COBOL was the first high-level language (developed by a 
>committee funded by the Department of Defense) and has been around, like, 
>forever.

A minor quibble.  My knowledge of these things is, admittedly, limited 
but I recall being taught that FORTRAN predated COBOL.  According to 
http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fortran :

--begin quoted text:

The first manual for FORTRAN appeared in October 1956, with the first 
FORTRAN compiler delivered in April 1957.

--end quoted text

... and from http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cobol :

--begin quoted text:

COBOL was initially created in 1959 by The Short Range Committee, one of 
three committees proposed at a meeting held at the Pentagon on May 28 and 
29, 1959, organized by Charles Phillips of the United States Department of 
Defense (exactly one year after the Zurich ALGOL 58 meeting).

[snip]

This subcommittee completed the specifications for COBOL as the year of 
1959 came to an end.

--end quoted text

... and note the reference to 'the ZURICH ALGOL 58 meeting'... although no 
compiler seems to have resulted from that.

(The formulation I generated, e'er-so-long ago, was 'FORTRAN is the Royal 
Tongue, COBOL is the Noble.')

DD

This will depend upon how your (mainframe) shop has programmer tasks set up. 
HOWEVER, in general, you won't be able to compile or test or do anything else 
with your COBOL source code unless you understand the basics of JCL.  You may 
(or may not) be able to do QMF all "interactively" - but if you company wants 
you to set up "canned" inquires for future use, then yes, you will probably need 
JCL for that too.

Bottom-Line:
  It sounds as if you are being asked to do a LOT of stuff that you don't have 
the training for.  Either your company needs to commit resources (like money) to 
get you trained or to hire someone (possibly a contractor) to get you "started".

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: advice on books to learn cobol

- **From:** "some" <s@mailinator.com>

```

"some" <s@mailinator.com> wrote in message 
news:1162514276.494076.237310@i42g2000cwa.googlegroups.com...
> Hi All,
>
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
> I don't know such basic things am I too dull?).

It is not dull or stupid to not know something; it IS dull or stupid to not 
WANT to know it.

You have shown by your posts here that you really want to learn what is 
required.

You are engaged in formulating a plan of action to acquire the knowledge you 
need.

Far from being dull, this is commendable.

>
> If I tell them that resources are needed they will instantly remove me
> considering me lazy,incapable and unfit for the job.

I seriously doubt that, but they may project this attitude in order to keep 
their employees in line... (As long as they can persuade people to believe 
this, they can pay minimum wages, provide minimal benefits, and keep people 
at their desks. It lloks like 'good business' but long term it is 
disastrous. Besides, anyone who is remotely bright or passionate about their 
work will move to another company as soon as they can. Repressive regimes 
(in companies, no less than in politics) cause the people who can do so, to 
go elsewhere, and leave the 'dead wood' to run the business.)

If you are right about this, then you might do well to look for another 
company where they value enthusiasm and loyalty. An employer whose 
underlying attitude is that staff are lazy and incompetent is not one where 
you would want to spend your career. (They are unlikely to be in business 
for the long haul, anyway...)

Where are you working (not the Company, the country)? Is there such a 
surplus of IT people that they can be easily and instantly replaced?

Any reasonable employer would be glad to have the truth. If resources are 
needed then there are only 2 options:

1. provide them.
2. don't provide them.

If they opt for 2 above, as you believe they will, they then have to start 
recruitment. It is a costly process, even if they can immediately find 
someone who has what they want, and is available to start right away. Every 
week that goes by is costing them money and slipping the work. It will cost 
them more to recruit someone than to assist you with your self-learning.

If you have been with them for more than 6 months, you will have acquired 
local knowledge that is valuable to them even if you DON'T have the specific 
skill they need right now. Firing you would be a very stupid move. 
Encouraging you and helping you has the best payoff for all concerned.

You have 5 years in IT; don't let them undermine your confidence.


>They will bring in
> somebody who has done such things before and claim it is my fault that
> I don't know things.

No, they won't.  (Even if they did, they would still have to buy the tools 
for the job...)

If that is how they operate you really shouldn't be there... I honestly 
believe you are letting your insecurity (which they obviously orchestrate 
and play on) affect your thinking.

I'd schedule a meeting with the department head and tell him you are doing 
your best to acquire what is needed, as quickly as possible. However, some 
of the software you are required to demonstrate knowledge of is expensive 
and cannot be obtained for nothing. This is true whether they get an expert 
in the subject or let you proceed with your learning project. Give them a 
bottom line -say 'several thousand dollars' - and tell them that, while you 
can easily acquire the knowledge, that is what the tools are going to cost. 
They should decide if they are serious about doing this before proceeding.


>So, either I learn things on my own quite fast or
> lose my job.
>

Usually when one door closes, another door opens... leaving this job or 
getting fired might be a very good career move...


> I understand there are lot of experienced programmers in this group and
> could learn from them. What is the proper method to be able to learn as
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>

1. Be honest. (Even if they are not...)
2. Let them decide whether they want to proceed, given that doing so will 
require expenditure.
3. Apply yourself to learning. (The more skills you can acquire, the better 
for your career...irrespective of what they decide to do)
4. Understand that companies incur a cost of operation. You are NOT wrong to 
tell them they need to spend money. Get quotes for software and let them see 
that you are not making it up.
5. After 5 years + of programming you are not a junior; there is enough of a 
track record there for you to get another job. Don't let them bully you or 
intimidate you; you are worth what they are paying you and if they fire you, 
you can certainly get another job. (Personally, I'd be looking anyway...)


> Thanks for your help and time.
>

Best of Luck,

Pete.
```

me 'Hey, you're lucky we gave you a job!' my response is along the lines

may all-of-a-sudden decide to outsource their IT, they may be acquired by 
another company which centralises IT in a different location, there may be 
a flood that destroys your work-site and you'll get laid off pending

suddenly and unexpectedly find yourself job-hunting.

```
Some,

Doc has responded with his experience and observations. They are very sound 
and match my own.

I would suggest you take his advice.

Some very quick responses below...

"some" <s@mailinator.com> wrote in message 
news:1162527850.699274.80000@f16g2000cwb.googlegroups.com...
> Hi All,
>
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> will believe my previous employer rather than me.

I am often in the position of recruiting project teams, and sometimes, 
permanent employees.

I back my judgement based on how they interact in the interview, how 
straight they are in answering straight questions, and their general 
attitude and approach. (Honesty, as I mentioned elsewhere, is very 
important. I'm not bothered if somebody doesn't know something; I'm very 
concerned if they try to pretend they do...)

While references are often required as part of the recruitment process 
(usually laid down by HR, who have nothing better to do...) I don't 
personally value them very much at all. (See separate new thread on this.)

I can remember one occasion many years ago when I was fired from a permanent 
programming job and told I would never work again and my career in IT was 
over. (The guy who fired me was a vindictive bastard who is now dead, so I 
guess I shouldn't say anything further about him...). The point was that I 
went to an interview and told them I had been fired. I explained what had 
happened (it had nothing to do with competence or ability; I had caused 
embarrassment to the guy who fired me, and I didn't even do it on 
purpose...).  That was 35 years ago and I have worked in IT ever since 
(never been fired since then, though... :-))

Your former employer has no more credibility than anyone else; present your 
case in the interview and get the job on merit. (Sometimes it helps to take 
samples of work you have done... program listings, documentation, etc. and 
use them to show your competence. (Don't leave any of this material behind; 
take it with you when you leave the interview.))

>
> My company is using IT as a support and does not want to spend
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> depend on me which makes things harder without a job.

When you have responsibility to others it does increase the pressure and it 
raises your insecurity. Unscrupulous employers will play on this. You have 
five years of IT, you have the right attitude, you deserve a better deal 
than you are getting. It is all about confidence. You know what you can do; 
nothing anyone (including your current employer) says about you, can change 
your ability.

>
> Anyway, back to my previous question can anybody please suggest how
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> Thanks a lot for your help,time and encouragement.

I have used QMF many years ago and found it useful then. I'm sure it is even 
better now. However, I believe there is still no substitute for good ol' SQL 
:-) You have this skill, so whether you manage to get your head round QMF or 
not, you can still provide the queries they are looking for. The point is 
that it is results you are measured by, not how well you know a particular 
tool. (Actually, I don't believe you'll have any problem using QMF; again, 
it comes down to confidence. Yours is being undermined by the lack of 
support from your employer and the stresses you have in your personal life. 
Many of the things you are worried about are shadows; concentrate on what 
you have already achieved, and know that whatever happens, you have the 
skill and knowledge to survive it. If your current employer doesn't 
recognise your value, someone else will.

Pete.
```

Similar. I once was fired for reasons other than competence (I asked, 
privately and politely, of a vice president that he not criticize me in 
front of my subordinates. He told me he would criticize me any damn time he 
felt like it. "Okay, I said. Fair's fair. Criticize me or my work in front 
of a crowd and expect the same in return." He fired me. Man had absolutely 
no sense of humor.).

Anyway, a couple of days later he called me at home, complaining about my 
unemployment claim and said that he would have to give prospective employers 
a bad recommendation unless I withdrew the unemployment claim. I told him if 
he lied about my work, I'd hit him so fuckin' hard his mother would die.

I never had any intimation that my former company delivered anything but 
glowing reports.
```

```

"Alistair" <alistair@ld50macca.demon.co.uk> wrote in message 
news:1162670549.614102.290000@e3g2000cwe.googlegroups.com...
>
> Pete Dashwood wrote:
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
> infringement.

Yes, there is a risk of that. That's why I qualified it with "sometimes"... 
You need to carefully assess what you take, and to whom you show it. It 
would be really stupid to take something that was obviously 'Company 
Private" and show it to the competition at an interview...

Nevertheless, in the early days of my career I did find it useful to take a 
few COBOL listings along when being interviewed for permanent programming 
positions.

There would be no reason why you shouldn't 'edit' these if they were 
sensitive. The object is to show that you can write the language and have 
done so in a real environment. The same would apply to C++ or Java or 
anything else.


>Also, what is to stop Joe Whizz from inserting his name
> at the top of a compile deck and passing Pete Dashwood's work off as
> his own?
>
ROFL!  (Joe is obviously far too stupid to be employed by ANYBODY... :-))

Reminds me of the story about Bernouilli (I think it was...) recognising an 
anonymous solution from Isaac Newton by exclaiming: " I recognise the Lion 
by his paw...!"

In my experience, people who write COBOL have their own individual 
idiosynchrasies and unique styles.

Sometimes I have worked in places and come across a listing that looks like 
I wrote it... It usually turns out it was someone who worked with me, or was 
trained by me. On one occasion I was able to contact a long lost friend who 
had done a contract at the same company and left before I arrived. I saw his 
code, recognised it was someone I knew, and made enquires which led to a 
phone number and a very alcoholic reunion... :-)

I would actually be extremely flattered if anyone tried to get a job by 
using my code, but I fear the jig would be up for them as soon as they had 
to write something new...

Pete.
```

```
As most of us who have worked with COBOL (especially on IBM mainframes) know, 
the subject of "Report Writer" is often almost as controversial as "paragraphs" 
vs "sections".  In the middle 80's, I went from "application programmer" to a 
"training" position - for a company (phone company) that was moving a bunch of 
NON-computer managers to COBOL application programmers.  During the course, I 
taught the FULL language - including internal SORTs (with input/output 
procedures) *AND* report writer.  A few years later, I became a systems 
programmer - so I would (occasionally) see application code from many groups. It 
always "amused" me when I would see RW code and be able to trace it back to one 
of my trainees, then (as time went by) I would see more and more as OTHER 
application people finally saw what RW could do for them.
```

<quote>
When Joe, a contractor with "an intense knowledge of .NET and SQL Server" 
and "acclaimed web development skills", was brought in, Josh and his 
coworkers thought they'd try something a little different. Instead of gripe 
and complain about his ineptitude, they'd create The Joe Board.

The Joe Board was simply a large whiteboard hung up in Josh's office. The 
goal was to see how much white space they could fill up with "Joeisms" 
before Joe's contract would inevitably be terminated early. Amazingly, and 
despite the fact that Joe was let go only four weeks after his three-month 
contract started, they ran out of whiteboard space. Following are some their 
favorite Joeisms ...

* How do I pass a string to a function?

* How can I write a SQL INSERT statement?

* That sucks! So, every time I change the code, I have to recompile?
</quote>

"Howard Brazee" <howard@brazee.net> wrote in message

    Sometimes they just want to fake it and get paid, without any plans of

http://thedailywtf.com/forums/40043/ShowPost.aspx
<quote>
Heidi S and Michael Hanson's employer was building an enterprise 
shipping/warehousing system but didn't have enough in-house resources to do 
it. One of the contractors they brought in to help fill the gaps was Paula, 
an "experienced Java programmer with strong knowledge of the shipping 
industry." For the first few months, things seemed to be going pretty well. 
At the weekly status meetings, Paula would report that good progress had 
been made and things were looking good for the deadline.

But as the deadline loomed closer, Paula reported that she was running into 
a lot of difficulties and would need some additional resources to finish up 
her piece. When Heidi and Michael came in to help, they realized gross of an 
understatement "some" was. Following is all of the code Paula had written 
for the application ...

    package test;

    public class paulaBean {

      private String paula = "Brillant";

      public String getPaula() {
        return paula;
      }
    }
</quote>

For those who don't speak Java, I'd imagine that's more or less equivalent 
to this COBOL code:

IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
PROGRAM-ID. paulaBean.
DATA DIVISION.
  01 paula PIC X(8) VALUE "Brillant".
PROCEDURE DIVISION.
  DISPLAY paula
  .

And this was after "the first few monthS", emphasis on the plural.

    - Oliver
```

Another interesting anecdote, Oliver.

I make no comment on Paula; but I have some observations about the people 
who worked with her...

1. How come none of her peers knew what she was doing?
2. Why was there no project management in place?
3. Any manager who simply accepts in a meeting that "everything is going 
fine" without actually looking, is an idiot. Once you have established 
credibility by delivering good quality product on time, then you can be cut 
more slack; until then (especially with a new contractor) regular friendly 
chats and perusal of code are the order of the day.
4. If this happened as part of a Programme I was responsible for (and it 
wouldn't), I'd fire the project manager concerned. But then, if proper 
project management had been in place, the situation could not arise.

I had someone who tried this on a project I was managing some time back. I 
didn't get to interview the person concerned; it was done by HR who decided 
she was dressed nicely so she should be OK... :-) The contractor concerned 
was fired within 2 weeks. (I actually did the work this person was supposed 
to be doing until I could get a replacement). Everything was delivered on 
time.

(These days I insist on building my own project teams (from both permanent 
and contract resources), insofar as this is possible, unless there is a 
really compelling reason the customer has for not doing so. Usually, because 
I get to do the projects that are considered "difficult and critical", they 
indulge me. Even if it is necessary to "inherit" existing staff, proper 
management is applied.)

Paula (and her ilk) are certainly culpable; but the people who employ them 
and don't manage them are no less so.

Pete.

```

"Alistair" <alistair@ld50macca.demon.co.uk> wrote in message 
news:1163094114.064153.40170@k70g2000cwa.googlegroups.com...
>
> What is not
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> up with.

    I agree, though it's difficult for someone with no programming 
background to evaluate the the programming skills of a candidate. You could 
have your other programmer employees evaluate the candidate, but if you're a 
small company just starting out, how do you evaluate the skills of the first 
programmer you hire?

>
> Incidentally, I have read reports that indicate that a minimum of 25%
> of cvs contain lies (such as job title bloat).

    One problem is that it's very difficult to be specific about your skill 
level, and very, very, very easy to be vague. For example, I know some 
COBOL. I definitely know more COBOL than any of my programmer friends, who 
got jobs making video games in C++, for example, but probably much less 
COBOL than any of the regulars in this newsgroup. So would it be unethical 
to write on my CV that I "know COBOL"? That I "know some COBOL"? That I 
"know a little bit of COBOL"? That I "have read and understood a lot of 
COBOL, but have little experience writing it"?

    And have I really read that much COBOL? I'm not sure. I've read a couple 
of language reference (from RM, IBM and others) which each provide examples 
of every statement, and I've read some "real world" COBOL programs as part 
of a project the company here, Castor Tech, is undertaking, and I've read 
through some of the NIST test suite (e.g. to figure out why my COBOL parser 
wasn't working properly for some specific files), and snippets from this 
newsgroup. Is that enough?

    The most honest would be to repeat all the above, but I consider my 
knowledge of COBOL to be relatively minor compared to, say, my knowledge of 
Java or PHP or object oriented design, etc. I could spend a paragraph or two 
on COBOL, but the advice I've heard recommends keeping your CV under 2 
pages.

    That said, there's a line to be drawn somewhere, and Paula and Joe (from 
the two anecdotes I copied and pasted so far) crossed it. They obviously 
lied about their abilities.

    - Oliver

```

"Oliver Wong" <owong@castortech.com> wrote in message 
news:QkL4h.19194$Xz6.65148@weber.videotron.net...
>
> "Alistair" <alistair@ld50macca.demon.co.uk> wrote in message 
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
> of the first programmer you hire?

You agree an initial trial period (3 months is fair) so that both parties 
can decide if there is a joint future. Goals are agreed and set, progress 
towards them is monitored, the company does everything it can to ensure the 
employee succeeds (proper tools and environments are in place, working 
conditions are pleasant and reasonable); the employee strives to establish 
credibility by achieving the agreed goals. After three months, the rate goes 
up, and the new employee is now a valued member of staff whose expertise can 
be called on when employing more people.

(I once offered to work one month for free so as to establish credibility. 
It is important for both employees and employers to do this... At the end of 
the month they offered me a one year contract and I negotiated a rate that 
covered the revenue I lost in the first month. I ended up being there for 2 
years...

I also once did a short term job where I offered to do it for free and take 
the money I saved them on the first month's billing. It was an offer I made 
in a bar on the South Coast of England (I think Jack Daniel was probably 
whispering in my ear :-), to a CEO who was moaning about how expensive IT 
was and how he couldn't afford to employ "guys like me" (as if there are any 
:-)). He was buying an IT service that was costing a fortune. I went into 
his place, worked for 4 days re-organising some procedures and data storage, 
and writing some new ones, and trusted him to keep his part of the bargain. 
A few weeks later I received a substantial cheque, being the difference 
between his bill this month and last month.

Then there was the famous time when I offered the CEO of a major UK company 
his money back (he really pissed me off with his denigration of IT generally 
and contractors in particular, so I rashly made this offer in a fit of 
pique...:-) if the project did not go in on time and on budget. It was a 9 
month job and 24 hours before the deadline we still weren't quite there... I 
have never forgotten the support that team gave me and the fantastic job 
they did so that we met the dealine with 6 hours to spare... (My house was 
on the line... I always honour deals.)

These days, I'm more sensible and would offer a trial period on a lower 
rate, if it was a job I REALLY wanted to do.

The point is that credibility must be established and there is nothing to 
stop you using your imagination to do so...


>
>>
…[18 more quoted lines elided]…
> files), and snippets from this newsgroup. Is that enough?

I think you have to consider what a prospective employer is looking for. 
They want someone to write COBOL in their environment (for example). OK, how 
confident do you feel that, with everything you outlined above, you can meet 
this requirement?

If you think you can do it, then it is fair for you to claim COBOL 
expertise. You may not know EVERYTHING that someone who has worked for them 
for a couple of years knows (you certainly won't have the business 
knowledge) but if you are the kind who learns quickly, knows how to find out 
stuff really well and is confident of the basic skill set, then you will 
probably be an asset them.

(If I was looking for a COBOL person and you were available, I'd employ you 
in a heartbeat, Oliver :-))

There is no need to lie on a CV. There is a need to balance what you have 
done and what you can bring to the prospective job.

All too often prospective employees agonise over the intimate details of 
technical environments,and what they actually DID there, where the Company 
simply has a requirement. Can you do it or can't you? That is the ONLY thing 
that is really important.

This is why companies (and pimps) write ridiculous job requirements; they 
don't understand the tech world so they throw in everything they have heard 
mentioned on the shop floor, or read in this week's Computer Weekly or 
airline magazine, in case it is relevant.

"COBOL programmer needed. Must have Bendix OS/4 and Sunbeam online 
communications experience."

Oh well, I guess all those years of writing COBOL on IBM across 5 different 
OSes and using CICS, are pretty irrelevant... Hope they find someone...

What did they really want? Someone who could maintain their existing COBOL.

Could you do it? All day long, with one hand tied behind your back...

How do you get the job? Meet them, listen to them, show them what you can 
bring to the party.

(I know, the first barrier is the pimp, who doesn't want to be seen putting 
someone up who is not EXACTLY what they asked for, and who has no idea how 
to decide...)

Under these circumstances, I wouldn't blame someone for writing that they 
had knowledge of Bendix and Sunbeam on their CV. Yeah, I know it is not 
strictly kosher (and I've never done it) but, as an employer I wouldn't hold 
it against them... If you would have trouble sleeping nights after doing 
this, then make it true; do some homework on Bendix and Sunbeam so that you 
can at least understand where they are coming from.

Bottom line: If it gets you an interview, go for it. You can assess how 
important this requirement REALLY is when you talk to them.)
>
>    The most honest would be to repeat all the above, but I consider my 
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> under 2 pages.

Mine is 36 pages. I have a 7 page summary of highlights. I only produce the 
full one at an interview, and only if they ask me. It is scrupulously 
honest, and is an interesting chronicle of a lifetime in IT.

Having said all of that, I don't disagree with your 2 page rule. Certainly, 
it is MUCH better to have 2 pages that are really pertineint to a specific 
job than to have 30+ pages that cover everything.

This being the case, I sometimes extract from my full one and prepare a two 
or three pager showing why I am suitable for a specific job.

Again, it is important to assess what they are actually looking for, then 
decide whether you are confident enough to apply for it.
>
>    That said, there's a line to be drawn somewhere, and Paula and Joe 
> (from the two anecdotes I copied and pasted so far) crossed it. They 
> obviously lied about their abilities.

They lied about their skill sets; we simply don't know about their 
abilities...

Not having the ability to do something because you haven't been properly 
trained or haven't learned about it, does not mean you have no ability. It 
simply means you don't have that skill set.

Lying about it and then perpetuating that lie for financial gain, simply 
shows you have learned the wrong lessons in Life, and your world view is 
fucked.  Readjustment will occur over time, and it will be painful...

Pete.
```

"Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
>
> You agree an initial trial period (3 months is fair) so that both parties 
> can decide if there is a joint future.

Use caution. In some jurisdictions (California, for one, France, for 
another), employment is not "at will" and, once hired, the difference 
between an employee and a barnacle is not great. That is, it is against the 
law to terminate an employee absent some egregious flaw, such as a 
propensity toward arson or collecting kitten heads. Come to think on it, the 
flaw probably has to be work-related.

What this means, in practice, is that you have to hire ANOTHER employee to 
kill the first one. Being a manager requires certain skill sets not normally 
found in those at the lower levels.
```

application area that was simply money in the bank, once you had it on a CV.

That is just awful. I don't know why/how companies get themselves into this 
state. To me, it simply reflects bad practice by insecure managers.

(My Project Management book is moving towards completion on the "back 
burner" in the spare time that I seldom have, and it discusses the 
importance of open and free communication by all concerned, if success is to 
be achieved. I also look at why this doesn't happen and what to do about it. 
It is a fascinating area; I believe that if people are to work for you, the 
least you can do is be honest and up front with them. Nothing good is 
achieved by withholding information or having secrets. "Company Private" 
information is one thing; political gossip, control by stifling information, 
and deliberate misinformation is quite another.)
>
> The contract was for three months... I accomplished the task (upon which
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>

The very first contract I ever did in the U.K. was with Seagrams, the famous 
whisky distillers in Bedford. I was pretty excited and much more naieve than 
I am today (it was 1976). The pimp was a fairly decent person as pimps go 
and was struggling to get his new agency off the ground. He dropped me off 
at the client on my first day and I got stuck in right away, eager to reward 
his faith in me. It was a six month contract and involved maintaining some 
thousands of COBOL programs to accommodate a changed business process. 
(yeah, I know... :-). It was necessary to locate every place in the program 
where it did a certain thing, then change it so it did it differently... By 
the third day I was going nuts, so I spent three more days writing a COBOL 
program to process the source code and make the changes. I was pretty 
pleased with myself for having achieved six months work in two weeks, and 
couldn't understand the horror and disbelief when I told the pimp... I was 
lucky in a way, because he realised I hadn't yet got the hang of this 
contracting lark, and managed to place me somewhere else fairly quickly, 
after having a talk and explaining that the idea was not to excel but to be 
on site for as long as possible... :-)  Over time, I gradually realised that 
these two goals are not mutually exclusive; if you excel, companies are 
often encouraged to give you more work of a more "interesting" nature, and 
even if they have nothing in the short term, they are likely to contact you 
in the future when they do. It comes down to credibility, as I mentioned 
elsewhere.

Yes, I agree it does, Doc. Not all employers have the imagination or courage 
to depart from standard procedure, but when you find one who looks as if he 
might, the results can be very... "entertaining" :-)

Pete.

Until such time as a Managerial Decision is needed - said Decision being a

work *for* anyone, Mr Dashwood.  I am a consultant, I work *with* people.

…[3 more quoted lines elided]…

>where it did a certain thing, then change it so it did it differently... By 
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…

No.  No.  NO.  The idea is to do what the client has told me it wants and 
what I enjoy doing... and if I am not enjoying it then it should be 
minimally distressing... and if it is more than minimally distressing then 
it is time for me to find another contract.  The more I say 'I'm having 
Fun!' the more others, in my experience, say - often with a bit of 
confusion or trepidation - 'But... you're doing Good Work.'

This once lead to a curious interaction.  I was on a contract and I 
realised that things would be better if I left; I contacted my pimp and 
told him that he had first stab at placing me but if he didn't have 
anything promising I would be 'floating my papers'.

He was furious... and pointed out a clause in the contract that held *me* 
liable for 'lost potential income' or something of the sort; the gist of 
it was that if the pimp said that the client had said that the client had 
wanted me and I was not willing to work then I owed the pimp the balance 
of the contract.

I said that I understood the clause but that we were both Reasonable Men 
and could understand that maintaining me at that site was not in anyone's 
interest... his response was 'If I say they said they wanted you and 
you're not there then you owe me the balance on the contract.'

I replied that it was all up to him... that he could either not hold me to 
that clause and call up the client at 9:am the next day, saying that I'd 
had an unspecified Family Emergency and that he was working on getting a 
replacement in, you know how these things happen...

... or I would show up at work at 10:am and, with quiet dignity and 
professional manner and language, tell my manager and his director what I 
*really* thought of them, the company's culture, the project, the work 
environment... and the weather, for that matter; by the time I was done 
one of them would be calling the pimp *demanding* I be taken out of 
there...

... and he, the pimp, would *never* stand a chance of placing another 
person with this organisation *ever again*.

'You wouldn't do *that*!'

'As sure as you'd hold me to that clause, I would... as I said, we are 
Reasonable Gentlemen, do you think you can notify them of my Family 
Emergency?'

[snip]

>> and my response has been 'I've studied a bit of mathematics in my time,

'Sweet like a razor', Mr Dashwood... I aspire to that goal, sometimes I 
make it.

DD

```

"Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>

>> How interesting, Mr Dashwood.  I've found myself in situations where a
>> prospective client has looked at my bragsheet and mused 'Well, you don't
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
>

I was taught in the Dale Carnegie Sales Course that people seldom give the 
real reason for a rejection but, instead, give as a reason something more 
plausible. I was further taught that you can often smoke out the real 
reason. For example:

You: "If I COULD meet your delivery time of two weeks, is there any other 
reason preventing you from signing up right now?"
Prospect: "Well, the price is a little higher...."
You: "Ah! So, if I could meet your price threshold, then delivery is not 
such a big deal. Right?"

and so on...

In practice, it goes like:

Me: "So, if I didn't live with my mother, you and I could, uh, you know?"
Me: "So, if I didn't live with my mother and had a job, we could..."
Me: "So, if I didn't live with my mother, had a job, and was not completely 
bald..."
```

I was alway a fan of Classic Interview Question Number 327: 'You have a 
transaction file containing customer number, part number, quantity 
purchased and total cost.  Your master file has customer number, part 
number, quantity purchased and total cost for the last five transactions 
for this particular part number.  Write the code for the standard 
match update; if the transaction file has a customer or customer/part 
number combination not found on the master create a new record and if the 
master record has all five transactions filled roll off the first and put 
the update numbers last.'

(if the prospective worker asks 'The master file... is it sequential or 
indexed?' they pass, period, without writing any code)

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: advice on books to learn cobol

_(thread depth: 12)_

- **From:** "Charles Hottel" <chottel@earthlink.net>
- **Date:** 2006-11-03T04:31:10+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<iCz2h.1732$l25.605@newsread4.news.pas.earthlink.net>`
- **References:** `<1162105054.088570.244330@m7g2000cwm.googlegroups.com> <ei7i3c$dl0$1@web.aioe.org> <1162400311.788159.253160@i42g2000cwa.googlegroups.com> <12kik1ef4uk4fa2@news.supernews.com> <eicva9$2m7$1@reader2.panix.com> <1162493027.399737.249490@m73g2000cwd.googlegroups.com>`

```

"some" <s@mailinator.com> wrote in message 
news:1162493027.399737.249490@m73g2000cwd.googlegroups.com...

<snip>
 Also do I need to know
> JCL(Job Control Language) a lot for working on a mainframe or just the
> basics would be enough?
>
> Thanks a lot.
>

I think the best books on JCL are by Gary Deward Brown.  The Mike Murach 
website also has a good JCL book.

I don't know much about QMF.

So how long do you think you have to learn COBOL, DB2, QMF, and JCL?  One 
week for each? Two weeks each tops? Don't get overwhelmed. You can't eat an 
elephant in a day. Try to get them to tell you what is most important and 
what is less important so you can prioritize your learning processes. There 
is a lot of experince here that can help but most people won't hand it to 
you without first seeing that you have made some effort yourself. That is 
just one of the ways of the world. Look at this as a great opportunity to 
learn new things, broaden your experience and make yourself invaluable to 
you employer.  There are alot of unemployed and employed guys that would die 
for a chance to work on this type of application and environment.

As a trainee programmer whose only experience was programming in college I 
spent the first three months on my first programming job learning COBOL, DOS 
JCL and IBM mainframe concepts.  Most of this was from programmed 
instruction books and videos. DOS JCL was easier to learn that MVS JCL. At 
the end that time I could begin work on the easier COBOL programs.  Of 
course back then we had nor source code editors only a keypunch machine. JCL 
sounds simple at first as there are just a few different statements. Data 
definition (DD) statements are used to connect you programs with your 
non-database files. The JCL manual has hundreds of pages describing all the 
various options. There are a lot of options to give you a lot of control. 
Most of the time you will use only a few.

On a CDC 6600 computer under the Scope operating system if you wanted a disk 
file you could say: REWIND DISK. If it already existed it was repositioned 
to the beggining. If it did not exist it would be created.

On z/OS if a catalogued disk file exists you would say something like: 
//ddname dsn=datasetname,disp=SHR
If it did not exist you would say something like: 
//ddname dsn=datasetname,disp=(new,catlg,delete),
                                                                             
                                        // 
dcb=(dsorg=ps,recform=ps,blksize=8000,lrecl=80),
                                                                             
                                        //              space=(........)
That would be pretty much a minimum.

A lot of work on mainframes is done under CICS - Customer Information 
Control System.  Have they mentioned that. This is used to build online 
systems, the so called "green screens" the you may have heard of. There is 
also something called Websphere used for server applications.  I did not 
have time to look at the DARS site very much but at: 
http://www.dars.muohio.edu/public/DARwinHardware.html  I saw AIX, UNIX, 
Windows, DARS mainframe and CICS mentioned. The last two links did not work 
so no joy there. At any rate DARS is a web has a web interface presumably 
seved with data from a mainframe, so you well may be doing onlinedevelopment 
on the mainframe and not batch development. You will still need to know JCL 
but not as much and a lot of the file I/O stuff I mentioned above probably 
won't be relevent as databases will be used and that is more in line with 
your current experience. The Mike Murach website has excellent CICS books. I 
don't know much about Websphere so I can't make any recommendations there.

Since you are experienced in C/C++ and they have structs that will help 
speed things up.  Files and file I/O on mainframes is definately involves 
different concepts.  There are records, blocking and access methods:

QSAM - Queued Sequential Access Method
    These can be fixed-blocked, variable-blocked or undefined format.

VSAM - Virtual Storage ACCESS Method comes in three flavors:
    ESDS - Entry Sequenced Data Sets
    KSDS- Keyed Sequential Data Sets
    RRDS - Relative Record Data Sets

This kind of I/O is diffrent from stream I/O.  You read files and you get a 
whole record at a time which you then process. You build records andwrite 
them to your output files. This will be one of the greatest differences.

If you will work mainly with databases then your knowledge of SQL will help 
greatly especially if you are familiar with embedded SQL.

Most data in a COBOL program is global in a WORKING-STORAGE SECTION not 
local.  There is a LOCAL-STORAGE SECTION but it is fairly new and I have not 
seen it used much. There are many ways to define and manipulate data. You 
will see a lot of things where you can make an analogy to C/C++ but there 
will be many quite different also.  Instead of calling functions you will be 
PERFORMing paragraphs. The command that operate on the data will be in a 
PROCEDURE DIVISION.  There are intrinsic function that work similarly to C 
functions but you cannot define your own functions that return a value 
inline as part of an expression. With various options and nested programs 
you can go a long way in that direction but I have never seen nested 
functions used very much. You will find rough equivalents:

PERFORM variants will do:  while/do ... until/for type constructs
IF/ELSE will do: if/else
EVALUATE is much better than switch
COMPUTE/ADD/MULTIPLY/DIVIDE will do the obvious
MOVE is quite powerful because the variable definitions use PICUTURE clause 
that can contain formatting characters

etc.

Good luck.
```

In article <1162614701.817460.305600@e3g2000cwe.googlegroups.com>,
some <s@mailinator.com> wrote:
>>Charles Hottel wrote:
>
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
>the best and has offered me the maximum help.

Wow... must have been really bad off, eh?

[snip]

>You are fully correct. But the issue is IT is viewed as a support chore
>in my company on which minimum money should be spent. Today, where
>people who are far more skilled than me and can work for fraction of my
>wages(due to outsourcing)  I was bit afraid of making the management
>unhappy lest they may outsource my job.

Short and sweet: if the worst thing comes to pass what do you have to 
lose... this 'wonderful' job?

>As you all have said my best
>option is to become more skilled and try for a different position where
>hopefully management is better. Another issue is company work takes
>80-90hrs/week and that leaves little time for gaining more
>skills,finding another job but I understand I need to find time.

That is what stops first.  You find a class, *any* class, that you want to 
take and you inform your boss that you need to leave at (time) on (these) 
days in order to attend class and at (other time) on (those) days to 
study and complete assignments so that you can learn the things that are 
expected of you to do your job.  One of two things will happen:

1) He will say yes... and you can either take the class or actually use 
the free time for something else.

2) He will say no... at which point you tell him 'fine, I quit' and go to 
pack up your desk.  You then respond to *anything* he says with 'I want to 
discuss this with you and HR (the Human Resources department)'.  You then, 
in the presence of a Personnell Person, ask how it can be that you are 
required to learn new things and then given neither the time nor the 
resources to learn them; any response other than 'here is the time, here 
are the resources' is met with 'I hate to disappoint you but that is 
unreasonable and impossible; I cannot work under those conditions and I'd 
like to get back to cleaning out my desk.'

In other words... don't let them fire you.  Quit.

[snip]

>Actually, I have heard a way to avoid such management issues is to 
>become a tenured faculty where people cannot play games with you after 
>you are tenured.

That has been reported as being incorrect.  Attributed to Heny Kissinger 
is the quotation 'Academic politics are so vicious because there is so 
little at stake.'

>Unfortunately, I don't have the qualifications for 
>that. To acquire the qualifications I need to take classes part-time as 
>quitting full time work is infeasible for me. 

Take the part-time classes and learn something work-related, use that to 
find a job in a better place, use the time that working in a better place 
frees up to learn more stuff that you enjoy... or so I would suggest.

> 
>Can anybody please advise if that would be a good decision?

It may be a good decision if it makes you happy... and Plato reports that 
Solon said 'Call no man happy until he is dead'.

DD
```

"Charles Hottel" <chottel@earthlink.net> wrote in message 
news:FS13h.2246$l25.1586@newsread4.news.pas.earthlink.net...
>
<snip>

> Some people have the temperment to be contractors and some don't.

That's for sure... and there's nothing wrong with either group.

>I am one who does not. Pete Dashwood does.

Contracting suits my life style. I have no responsibilities to anyone other 
than myself (and, indirectly, the people who pay me of course...) and I am 
by nature a survivor.  Contracting allows me to make a good living and work 
when I want to, rather than when I have to. (Most of the time... sometimes I 
do have to, because I see the coffers getting low and I have to take care of 
the little old guy who will be me in the not-too-distant future... :-), but, 
for the most part, I can afford to do the things I want)

Up until quite recently I have enjoyed travelling and experiencing other 
cultures (now, I just love to be at home and find it harder and harder to go 
to Europe, even though that is where I can best sell my skills...), so 
contracting was an ideal option.

Security, or the lack of it, has never been a consideration for me with 
regard to contracting or going permanent. I realised about 30 years ago that 
the only security any of us have is the couple of pounds of grey slush that 
sits in our skulls... There are no jobs for life and there haven't been for 
many years now. ANY company will fire its most loyal employees if the 
climate turns bad... I've seen it happen and I've seen it happen to people 
who were much better than me... It is a foolish illusion to believe that if 
you have a Government job you won't be fired; they can do much worse things 
to you (like, put you in a soul-destroying, boring, mind-numbing, job that 
will drive you to the edge of insanity if you stay there...).

For myself, I plan to enjoy the Summer here, then go back to Europe for a 
couple more years to generate enough cash to come home and retire. If I was 
to take another job in NZ (even on contract) it would take at least 6 or 7 
years to do that, so, whether I like it or not, travelling has to be on the 
cards again.


>He just had to leave a really good job, it was not his fault, just normal 
>politics, but it did not seem to upset him that much.

Well, I was sorry they cancelled the project as we came into the final 
phase, but I respect the right of Management to manage. It is their company 
and their money; I get paid to advise, and I gave them the best advice I 
could. Nobody had any doubt that our team would have delivered, but the 
strategic decision was not to proceed. These things happen; no point in 
getting unwrapped about it. I was offered another job in Auckland fairly 
quickly (pimps are amazing at sniffing opportunity :-)) but I decided to 
enjoy some time off.

This is the freedom that contracting can bring. I don't want to work until 
after the Summer; I don't have to. It gave me a chance to visit the Southern 
part of the USA and make the Holy Pilgrimage to Lynchburg, TN, where they 
distill Jack Daniels, who has been an acquaintance of mine for over 30 years 
now :-), and I was able to spend time with friends in the South and in Los 
Angeles on the way home. It would have been much harder to have this 
experience if  I was in full time employment. I saw some very interesting 
things on this trip and it also helped me to understand the feeling of 
ordinary Americans at this difficult time in the nation's history.

(I came home with a new computer that I couldn't get in NZ yet, and that 
alone made the trip worthwhile for me... :-))

I am too sensitive, perhaps my greatest fault, and it would have
> affected me.
>
We should never let our jobs define us; work is important, but life is more 
so.

> Have you considered working foe the federal or state government? They can 
> be pretty secure.

Sorry, Charles, I beg to differ... see above.

> No matter where you work a diversity of skills is you best protection 
> against being unemployed.
>
Absolutely and Amen!

> I think it hard to break into acedamia.

I got the impression Some is already close to the acadaemic environment. It 
MIGHT be an option for him, but I still believe his best option is ot get 
out of where he is...

Pete.

In article <1162595031.138956.301570@e3g2000cwe.googlegroups.com>,
some <s@mailinator.com> wrote:

[snip]

>Thanks a lot for your help. They told me to demonstrate I can do some
>work in QMF,COBOL,DB2.

Bingo.  Spring this trap in reverse on those who set it by informing them 
that you are a computer programmer and indefinite quantities are difficult 
to code for... rather than 'some work' you need specific tasks and goals 
to be accomplished.

(This will help avoid a common Management Dictum, where any amount 
requested is categorised as 'Too Much!' and any effort or accomplishment 
demonstrated is 'Not Enough!')

Ask what is it that they want to be able to see you do... and see how they 
respond.

>For JCL they told me it can be done after I have
>proven I can work in above mentioned tools(QMF,COBOL,DB2).

'Can work'... to what level of competence or complexity?  As was said by 
Beelzebub (as reported in the story 'The Master and His Pupil' (a 
retelling of 'The Sorcerer's Apprentice'), found in 'English Fairy Tales' 
by Joseph Jacobs, on the web at 
http://www.sacred-texts.com/neu/eng/eft/eft16.htm ) 'Set me a task!'.  
You're a programmer and you know the disappointments that can result when 
you're not working from specs.

DD
```

## Thread: COBOL FAQ — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Meta: FAQs, group policy, charter`](topics.md#meta)_

### COBOL FAQ

- **From:** wmklein@ix.netcom.com (William M Klein)
- **Date:** 2006-11-03T05:27:03+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,news.answers,comp.answers
- **Message-ID:** `<computer-lang/cobol-faq_1162531603@rtfm.mit.edu>`

```
Archive-name: computer-lang/cobol-faq
Posting-Frequency: twice a month
Last-modified: 2005/08/16
Version: 3.03
URL: http://home.comcast.net/~wmklein/FAQ/COBOLFAQ.htm
Maintainer: wmklein@ix.netcom.com (William M Klein)
  
                                COBOL FAQ
                      (Frequently Asked Questions)
    
    Last-Modified: Spring 2002
    
    The full (but quite out-of-date) COBOL FAQ can be viewed at:
    
		http://home.comcast.net/~wmklein/FAQ/COBOLFAQ.htm 
   
    If you have comments, corrects, deletions, or additions, 
    please send private email to:
    
        wmklein <at> ix.netcom.com
   
   
    This FAQ answers such questions as (and addresses topics such as):
   
     - Where can I get a COBOL compiler? 
     - Is there a free COBOL compiler? 
     - Where can I contact... ?
     - What about OO COBOL? 
     - Books about COBOL
     - COBOL Tools
     - What can/should I post in the COBOL newsgroups?
     - What about USAGE? COMP? Storage for data in xyz format? etc?
     - How do I get started with COBOL? Where can I get education? 
 		Tutorials? Etc
   
   	 and much, MUCH more
```

## Thread: OT: windoze woes and full rant mode is on — 116 msgs
