### OT: windoze woes and full rant mode is on

- **From:** "Charles Hottel" <chottel@earthlink.net>
- **Date:** 2006-11-03T16:53:12+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol

```
Why I hate being a systems programmer for my pc.

I apologize in advance for any bad formatting as I am typing this offline 
into Notepad and
will cut and paste it later which usually screws up the formatting.

Didn't Robert Duvall say in the Apocolypse Now movie that he loved the smell 
of sofware bloat
in the morning? If he didn't he should have.

If you don't like whining you may want to skip this, but if you are thinking 
of switching to
Internet Explorer 7 you might want to read that part to save yourself some 
grief.

In the last few weeks I have suffered a number of aggravations which I will 
now present in
order of increasing agravation.

Lowest Amount of Aggravation: MSN Messenger

I hate the MSN Messenger icon in my system tray. Microsoft Defender removed 
it but it came
back.  I stopped Outlook from starting it. Defender still thought it was 
gone so I used
msconfig to remove it from startup. It came back. I went to Outlook 2002 to 
try and stop it
from starting it. The help said: Tools, Options, Preferences should get me 
to the place to
turn it off. Except there is no Preferences tab. PC Magazine said to try: 
Tools, Options,
General. Yes the option is there and checked. All I need to do is uncheck 
it. Only it is
grayed out or yellowed out and I can't change it. PC Magazine said try: 
Start, Run then

RunDll32 advpack.dll,LaunchINFSection %windir%\INF\msmsgs.inf,BLC.Remove

but it said to be sure not to type any spaces as it could lead to 
unpredictable results, only
the string does contain spaces. Confused? Well me too as I only have a 
masters degree in
computer science from Johns Hopkins University and 35 years of experience 
with computers. I
know I am not even the smartest guy on this newsgroup and by a lot of potent 
brain power.

Anyway I found the above command string on the internet, tried it and it 
worked after the
reboot. I love rebooting all the time. Norton Antivirus 2006 starts up like 
a herd of turtles
in banana dust. So problem solved, only there was a windoze (I refuse to 
capitalize that word)
update for windoze messenger. Now I thought MSN Messenger and windoze 
messenger were differnt
programs just like Outlook and Outlook Express are different programs and 
windoze exploer and
 internet exploere are different..

I guess the Microsoft software naming guy is mentally challenged. But I 
digress. After installing windoze messenger
guess what was back? Well I killed it again so cross your fingers.


The next level of aggravation: Internet Explorer 7

How do I hate thee, let me count the ways.

windoze update installed this 14+ MB monster. I played with it trying to get 
the feel for the
user interface. I could not find any Help button. Try the upper right corner 
or press F1 like
I did. To get the Menu bar that has File, Edit, .. visible, right click on 
the command bar and
check Menu Bar. Help, Customize IE toolbars is your friend:

**********
"To show or hide toolbars

In Internet Explorer, right-click the Command bar to view the list of 
toolbars.
Do one of the following:
To show a toolbar, click the name of the toolbar to select it (a check mark 
will be displayed
beside it).
To hide a toolbar, click the name of the toolbar to clear the check mark."
**********

So now how do I read mail and read newsgroups?

**********
"To change buttons on the Command bar

In Internet Explorer, right-click the Command bar, point to Customize 
Command Bar, and then

click Add or Remove Commands.
Make one or more of the following changes:
To add a button, click the button you want to add in the Available toolbar 
buttons list, and

then click Add.
To remove a button, click the button you want to remove in the Current 
toolbar buttons list,
then click Remove.
To change the order in which buttons are displayed, click a button in the 
Current toolbar
buttons list, and then click either Move Up or Move Down.
To restore the Command bar buttons to their default settings, click Reset.
When you're done, click Close.
You should see your changes immediately. If you've added a lot of buttons, 
you might need to
resize the Command bar to see them all."
**********

Well I could not see any new buttons. There is a lot of open, wasted space 
available. There is
one whole line/bar with only one icon on it. There is empty space on the 
Command bar but no
new icons displayed.

*********
"To resize the Command bar

In Internet Explorer, right-click the Command bar, and then click Lock the 
Toolbars to clear
the check mark (if the check mark is already gone, skip this step).
Drag the Command bar separator bar  left or right.
When you're done, right-click the Command bar, and then click Lock the 
Toolbars."
*********

Well I just cannot see the Command bar separator which makes it hard to drag 
it:-(

On the right side of the Command bar just to the right of Tools there are 
two small greater
than signs: >>. Click them and a drop down list appers and then click Read 
email and you can
get your email.

So now how do you get to read your newsgroups?  Apparently there is no Read 
newsgroups button.
Searching the internet with terms like email or news, or newsgroups is like 
looking for a
single tree in a world wide forest.  Eventually I found a newsgroup on the 
microsoft web site
with the answer although it took me a while to figure out the details. This 
user interface is
a new low even by microshit standards.

Here is how you can read your newsgroups. Click Read mail as above. In 
Outlook click View,
Goto, News and you will get the newsreader you set in IE Explorer Tools, 
Internet options,
Programs tab.

That is as far as I got so far. One last thing. Since installing IE Explorer 
7 when windows
are maximized the leftmost letter is cut in half by the left edge of the 
window. Not just in
IE Explore but in ALL windows.

Stepping Up to the next level of aggravation: Backing Up my hard drive

I was backing up to DVD but it took a long time, it took 4 DVDs and I notice 
that some files
were not backed up because they were in use. Due to another aggravation 
which I am saving for
last my backup procedure became an area of intense focus. My last backup was 
made in June.

First I bought a Maxtor One Touch external hard drive. It generally works 
well but it does not
support backing up the windows folder or its subdirectories. To me this is a 
serious
deficiency, because if I had to reinstall windoze xp pro and then download 
all of the windoze
updates again over a slow dialup connection, it could take two and a half 
days of almost
continuous download. Unfortunatly this estimate is base upon actual 
experience:-----(((((((!!!

So I bought Symantec Norton Save and Restore(NS&R). This is getting way too 
long so I will
omit the gory details. It did not work. Some access to folder problems and 
three error
messages. Several hours learning more about xp security but not enough yet 
to fix the problem.
Contacted support. They said I need to log on as Administrator. Told them I 
already was. They
said I need to log on as Administrator. Apparently Symatec support consists 
of a computer or
human bot that finds error message codes in you email and sends you a canned 
email. I replyed
in ALL CAPS that I was the @#^^*(**^$#$**( ing Administrator. They gave me a 
lengthy process
of looking at two tabs in msconfig and diabling all services except MS 
services and Symantic
services including only programs and services on two lengthy lists. If I had 
followed these
instruction to a T I am pretty sure I would have lost the driver to my 
display and I could not
help but notice that NS&R was not on their list, only Norton Ghost. I got 
another access error
when I clicked ok.  On restart I saw that two of the services I had disabled 
were still there,
so probably something to do with them caused the error. I ran NS&R and got 
the same three
error messages as before and an additional one. Sent lengthy email to 
support detailing
everthing I did including list of services enabled and list of services 
disabled. They replied
that I need to log on as Administrator.

Sigggggggggggggggggggggghhhhhhhhhhhhhhhhh!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!

I replied with a strong message that contained no error message codes. They 
finally read more
of my previous lengthy email and said it was a windoze problem, they do not 
diagnose those and
I need to contact Microshit.

My reply: "Well I guess that lets you off the hook, huh?
Your company has my money and your software does not work. You win and I 
lose. Of course that
only works as a short term strategy.  Not that you or your company care but 
I will NEVER do
any more business with Symantec."

Catch-22. There is a refund page and a refund procees. It requires the 
original receipt. I do
not have it, because I send it in, to get the offered rebate which required 
the original
receipt. No joy there or here or wherever.

Higest Level of frustration: Trashing my hard disk

I get a newsletter from Internet Tourbus. They had a procedure for cleaning 
up your hard disk.
It seemed straightforward and appeared safe. At one point it involved 
running chkdisk. Even
though my computer is two years old it has a large hard drive 233GB. I do 
not know if that
matters or not. I do know that after I ran chkdisk my drive was trashed. It 
had a read error
in a critical place and windoze would not boot and using F8 did not work so 
no safe mode and
no nothing but a read error for me. Driver and recovery CD worked as boot 
source but none of
the recovery tools could do anything. Contacted Gateway non-support and was 
given a fdisk
command that did not work because he told me to use a forward slash in the 
path so I knew I
knew more than him. Reinstalled XP, downloaded windoze updates, reinstalled 
applications (not
all yet) and restored what was available from backup DVD. Repair saga 
continues.

Believe it or not I left out a lot of glitches that occurred during these 
events.

Sorry. I guess this is mostly me for me although I hope the Internet 
Explorer 7 part helps
some people. I just need to vent.

Leaving now to get car window replced as some vandal broke it out. I think 
thw word "window"
may be cursed and UNIX/Linux is looking better and better all this time. I 
wonder if my hard
disk is even large enough to hold Windoze vista.

#### ↳ Re: OT: windoze woes and full rant mode is on

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2006-11-03T17:39:44+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<eifut0$4fn$1@reader2.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<YtK2h.1898$0r.1534@newsread1.news.pas.earthlink.net>`

```
In article <YtK2h.1898$0r.1534@newsread1.news.pas.earthlink.net>,
Charles Hottel <chottel@earthlink.net> wrote:

[snip]

>So I bought Symantec Norton Save and Restore(NS&R). This is getting way too 
>long so I will
>omit the gory details. It did not work.

As a mainframe jockey my backup mantra is 'Incremental daily, system 
weekly'; I have been using the Acronis TrueImage software 
(http://www.acronis.com , the copy I have is of an older version (8.0)) 
and the only difficulties I have had involved getting files from an 
archive that had been made on another machine (file/folder permissions).

I formerly used Norton Ghost, which was fine for up to Win98... when I 
tried the XP version it seemed like they'd made it (Ghost) bloatware to 
the point where booting from the Restore disk (Norton proprietary, I 
believe) took fifteen to twenty minutes.  Acronis will allow you to make 
as many boot CDs as you wish; booting from one brings you into an 
environment where USB devices (ie, external drives) are recognised and a 
restore can be made to a blank HD.

This translates to - speaking from experience here - losing a hard drive 
at 2:pm, going to a computer store and getting a replacement drive (larger 
size than the original), booting from the Acronis CD - be prepared to 
navigate the GUI with the keyboard, the wireless USB mouse I have didn't 
seem to work well - selecting my restore and waiting about an hour.  By 
4:pm I was back up and running.

Must have 'bare metal restore' capabilities.  

(Every Sunday I do a full backup to a USB external drive and I then use 
Acronis' scheduling software to do an incremental at 11:47pm (2347hrs).  
The only nuisance is that I haven't found a way to automatically redirect 
the incremental backup script to the new archive so I have to do it 
manually.)

DD
```

- **Message-ID:** `<akluk25m7ru9r58fm2h7caj415r2h451pk@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<YtK2h.1898$0r.1534@newsread1.news.pas.earthlink.net> <eifut0$4fn$1@reader2.panix.com> <n6R2h.1808$ig4.1370@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net> <eii32f$deq$1@reader2.panix.com> <HK13h.2241$l25.158@newsread4.news.pas.earthlink.net> <eiiq7g$um$1@aioe.server.aioe.org>`

```
One solution is to always keep your most recent old computer.   Do
your back-ups to it, and test it.    You may have some licensing
problems, but this computer is only used as a ready-to-go backup.

The big advantage is you don't have to restore your applications to
work if your computer goes down.

You still need some off-site backup, which in my case is just data.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: OT: windoze woes and full rant mode is on

I use Acronis as  well.

I haven't set it up for my new Notebook yet as I am in the process of 
acquiring a high speed 200GB external drive for image copy.

The new machine (Sony Vaio AR250G) is superb and I'm having far too much fun 
with it to consider mundane things like backups... :-)

I've already encountered one problem: I needed to transfer a fair chunk of 
stuff from the old Pentium 4 Notebook to the new Vaio (Core 2 Centrino 64 
bit). My newly installed wireless LAN wasn't working properly so I connected 
the two machines using Firewire... (400MBS, about 8 times the maximum speed 
of wireless :-)). The Vaio was sucking data so hard that the Pentium 
overheated! It overheated so badly that it finally cut out before the 
transfer was complete... It was doing just under 3GB a minute; after around 
5 minutes the thermal cutoff tripped in and it simply stopped... The Vaio 
never even broke into a sweat :-) I finally got it to work by raising the 
Pentium 4 onto some books and using a large fan to keep air moving under it.

Sorry to see the problems you've been having, Charlie.

By coincidence, I also had trouble configuring Outlook 2003 for Newsgroups. 
I did what it said and installed the 'News' item onto the GO menu. It 
worked, but only for the first time I tried it! Next time I opened Outlook, 
the option was gone from the menu. I tried to repeat the process of 
installing it again but now the GO menu options didn't show it! I spent 
several hours before I sussed what was wrong. It involved a power struggle 
to be the default mail and News client between Outlook Express and Outlook. 
It was resolved when I let OE be the news client and Outlook everything 
else, but it wasn't fun and it was only trial and error that solved it.

I'm also considering IE 7 so I read with interest your cautionary 
experience. I'll post here how it goes when I get round to doing it.

Pete.

Thanks Steve, I'll take that on board.


> Firefox
> 2.0 is a far superior and far less bloated browser.  I would consider
> using that (which I do and have used for some time now)  rather than
> going anywhere near anything that starts with IE.

Yes, I tried Firefox last year and was favourably impressed. The problem I 
have is that I really need to support the MicroSoft environment because the 
stuff I develop is intended for it. There isn't much point in me developing 
a web based application then finding that it doesn't work properly on IE. (I 
can tolerate it working improperly on Firefox, even though I would prefer to 
have full cross-browser compatibility.) I am looking at purchasing 
MacroMedia's latest Studio 8  which really helps with this... but it is 
expensive and I need to close a few deals before I can justify it :-)


>
> Doc, I'm interested in your backup strategy.  I have a laptop with XP
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>

PMFJI, but yes, absolutely. I do that on my "old" Notebook using XP pro and 
a firewire connection. (You could also do it with USB, but it will be 
slower.)

The Notebook has a 40GB internal HDD and it is imaged to an exact duplicate 
external drive. If the Notebook drive failed I can swap the external drive 
into it in about 10 minutes, then replace the failed drive as the new 
external drive. The external drive is a 2.5", same as the internal, except 
it has a transparent plastic "harness" to enable the connections to it.

Acronis can copy track by track so that even hidden and "non-movable" files 
are copied.

I plan to do exactly the same with my new Notebook, as soon as the backup 
hard drive arrives...

Pete.
```

Firefox is a tabbed browser, has been for ages.  There are hundreds of
extensions some of which are tailored to suit the needs of developers.
Just add:

"""IE Tab - an extension from Taiwan, features: Embedding Internet
Explorer in tabs of Mozilla/Firefox.

This is a great tool for web developers, since you can easily see how
your webpage displayed in IE with just one click and then switch back
to Firefox."""

You can also get:

"""OperaView 0.6 by Bartosz Piec

Open pages in Opera from Firefox and Mozilla context menus. Very
usefull for web developers but not only!"""

I also run 'Web Developer', 'HTML Validator', 'NoScript' and a few more
which are useful for making web sites.

Safari nor any other browser your customers might use.

There is no excuse not to test your applications with IE, Firefox, &
Opera.

There is no excuse for large companies to fail to test with Safari and
Unix based browsers.

worlds' favourite?), etc. Oh, and don't forget, don't design in Flash
because many users still use 28k modems, don't use activex (security
issues) and many people disable Java and Javascript.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: OT: windoze woes and full rant mode is on

_(thread depth: 9)_

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2006-11-08T13:04:06+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4rcl7mFqq65eU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<YtK2h.1898$0r.1534@newsread1.news.pas.earthlink.net> <eifut0$4fn$1@reader2.panix.com> <4r3f9jFpdpc4U1@individual.net> <hehpk2hq7pk0q4arvstum7vhci5rhsvuo1@4ax.com> <4r50ghFpg38pU1@individual.net> <d2muk2l53uqhlbo7c53hj6mrv7s8u1ku6p@4ax.com> <12kuq2q4hrua0b8@news.supernews.com> <vsruk21da5vbef7sdmlpm0vc54atvnhke4@4ax.com> <1162924582.847762.316340@e3g2000cwe.googlegroups.com>`

```

"Alistair" <alistair@ld50macca.demon.co.uk> wrote in message 
news:1162924582.847762.316340@e3g2000cwe.googlegroups.com...
>
<snip
>>
>> Apparently they need multiple versions of I.E. as well.
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Thanks for reminding me about this, Alistair. I had honestly forgotten how 
difficult some people and organisations, who have probably never developed a 
web site in their lives, try and make it for those of us who do.

The fact is that, as a web developer, of course I want as many people as 
possible to see my sites and enjoy the experience of visiting. I'll take all 
reasonable measures to guarantee this, but if some are not able, then that 
is just too bad. Who suffers here? Only the Web Developer. To try and 
legally enforce measures to make the site more accessible is crazy. I don't 
discriminate against handicapped people in life and I wouldn't do so on a 
web site, but neither will I spend hours to ensure that any particular 
portion of this group can have access. If they can't see the pages, I'm 
sorry. There are accessibility features in Windows that may help. If they 
choose not to use Windows or use some other software that doesn't have those 
features, then that is entirely a matter for them.

By the same token, if an antiMS fanatic tells me I MUST make the site 
friendly to his particular flavour of Browser, and there is "no excuse" for 
not doing so, I would say I can immediately think of several excuses for not 
doing so... Being coerced would be the first one :-)

When people develop web sites they put in many hours of thought and effort 
to designing and building. They will use tools that help that process. Those 
tools are usually oriented to the platform where the site is being built, 
although products like Dreamweaver have had rudimentary facilities for cross 
browser testing for many years. Unfortunately, these tests are not always 
accurate, as I found to my chagrin during the last development exercise I 
undertook. The latest release of Dreamweaver (part of MacroMedia's Studio 8) 
apparently has rectified this and is much better at ensuring cross browser 
compatibility, but this is a very expensive tool.

Nobody developing a web site wants to limit the accessibility of it, either 
by browser or by any other limiting factor. It is a question of what is 
viable. If I embed an ActiveX control on my web server, there is no problem. 
If I try and download it to the client, there can be.  If I put JavaScript 
on a client page, some of the people viewing it won't see it as intended; if 
I replace it with ASP on the server and dynamically create the page, there 
should be no problem.

You could easily conclude that the best solution is probably to do 
EVERYTHING on the web server, then simply serve up a dynamically constructed 
page that suits the particular browser being used. This is the goal I am 
currently trying to reach, but it certainly isn't easy.

I will soon be undertaking a major web development effort and will use all 
the experience I have accumulated previously to try and attain this goal.

It isn't just about browsers, either. There is the question of what the 
Hosting ISP will allow... can I run COBOL CGI code? Does he support ASP, 
Java/VB Script on the server? Can I use MySQL or must it be SQL Server?

There is much more to it than the average person realises when they just 
find that their browser doesn't render a certain page correctly.

Web developers are probably never going to be all things to all people 
(except maybe for the very most trivial applications with static pages). I 
try to listen to the feedback I get and take it on board. But if it takes me 
100 hours to make something I have already built, visible to 15% of the 
audience for it, I'd rather invest that 100 hours providing better stuff for 
the 85%...

Truly it is written...

"For he that hath, to him shall be given: and he that hath not, from him 
shall be taken away even that which he hath."

(St. Mark, if I remember rightly...)

Pete.
```

I was reading along, and suddenly reeled back in horror. In a flash of 
light, it occurred to me that *some* people that do web applications do 
not run their own web servers.  Technical people, that is.  I cannot 
help but wonder, "why not?".  Setting up a web server is a relatively 
trivial exercise, and allows you to choose what you wish. Every facility 
you mention is Open Source, freely available software.

Unless the channel capacity requires heavy resources, there is little 
reason for a business not to host their own applications.

Even if they do need high capacity, that is more a matter of hardware, 
including line bandwidth, than it is of software.

> There is much more to it than the average person realises when they just 
> find that their browser doesn't render a certain page correctly.

Testing on different browsers is trivial, providing you have a machine 
with each.  Or a virtual machine with each.  You should be able to 
download those.

I also do not think it a matter of having to program for dozens of 
operating systems/browsers.  I think it more a matter of recognizing 
those tools sets which fall into the standard, and those that do not.

It may be more a matter of simply avoiding a few bad practices. Or 
specific tool-sets.

This reminds me of a bit I saw, years ago, done by a comedian standing in 
front of something that looked like a brick wall... he posited the Law of 
Synchronised Nuts.

Many folks who have visited an American city of any size have seen what 
the textbooks describe as 'A Nut'... someone manifesting what appear to be 
responses to the hallucinations of classic schizophrenia, usually.  The 
guy will be walking along, twitching and speaking in a rapid-fire manner 
to nobody that anyone else can see... 'You tell me I'm drunk?  Screw that, 
I'm not drunk, you can't tell me I'm drunk, I'm a Navy man, see, and 
*nobody* can tell a Navy man when he's drunk...'

Well... the comedian posited that in another city, say, fifty miles away, 
there was *another* Nut, carrying on the other side of the conversation... 
'Screw you, you're loaded... you were in the Army, those guys get tanked 
sniffin' the cork, I'll tell ya you're drunk any day of the week...'

DD

- **From:** Clark F Morris <cfmpublic@ns.sympatico.ca>

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<5hn3l2196sn3tu1lninfs7dt4oa0lh7gbm@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<YtK2h.1898$0r.1534@newsread1.news.pas.earthlink.net> <eifut0$4fn$1@reader2.panix.com> <4r3f9jFpdpc4U1@individual.net> <hehpk2hq7pk0q4arvstum7vhci5rhsvuo1@4ax.com> <4r50ghFpg38pU1@individual.net> <d2muk2l53uqhlbo7c53hj6mrv7s8u1ku6p@4ax.com> <12kuq2q4hrua0b8@news.supernews.com> <vsruk21da5vbef7sdmlpm0vc54atvnhke4@4ax.com> <1162924582.847762.316340@e3g2000cwe.googlegroups.com> <4rcl7mFqq65eU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
The postings below are for those who may not have followed the full
thread.

In the United States it is a requirement that all web-sites conform to
section 506 regulations of the Americans with Disabilities Act.  Very
briefly it means that a web-site must be accessible to people who are
blind or deaf or motion limited but a web site does not have to
provide for multiple disabilities.  The UN regulations at least used
to be the same according to the person from IBM who gave a SHARE
presentation on the topic back in 2001.  According to the experts in
the field, if the design is done up front and standards are followed
including use of certain data in the HTML tags such as descriptors for
graphics, this does not add much expense.  This also means being
sensitive to the use of colour because certain colour combination can
make a screen unreadable to people whose colour vision isn't good. You
should be able to navigate the screen by just using the keyboard. For
web-sites that are used for commercial, employment, educational or
means to access services, I can make a good case that if you believe
in access for those with physical challenges and enabling them to be
mainstream, then the force of law makes sense.

In general, I would say that paying attention to the standards for the
Internet and expecting as trailing edge a set of current
non-deprecated functions as feasible on the client should
automatically make the site usable to the majority of browsers.  I
know that I was not impressed when I had to download Macromedia Flash
to access the Microfocus web site.  I had the IT people at the client
site do it since it was the company's computer. 

In my case, I am more concerned about web-sites that require
unrequested pop-ups or software that I consider creates security
exposures on my machine.  I use Firefox as my primary browser because
it is moderately more secure.  I use Windows because it runs the
software I want.  If I get the energy, I will create a dual boot for
Linux on our home desktop or get a low powered one to play with.  I am
using Internet Explorer at work because that is what the client uses.
If what I was doing required a Mac, I would use that and would want
any web page I read using browsers there to work.  In a sense, it is
sort of like COBOL, if you want your program or web page to work
across platforms, don't use vendor extensions and if possible turn
them off in the development environment.  Also, if you are targeting
rural areas or people with lower income, make sure you page works with
28.8.  You won't be able to give them access to real-time audio or
video but they should be able to do most business comfortably.

Clark Morris

On Wed, 8 Nov 2006 13:04:06 +1300, "Pete Dashwood"
<dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:

>
>"Alistair" <alistair@ld50macca.demon.co.uk> wrote in message

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Web site compatibility was Re: OT: windoze woes and full rantmode is on

- **From:** LX-i <lxi0007@netscape.net>
- **Date:** 2006-11-11T21:34:47-06:00

    If you're using FireFox, a handy plugin is "nuke anything". It lets you 
right click on almost anything within the FireFox browser (paragraphs, 
floating boxes, images, flash animations, etc.), and choose "Remove this 
object", to cause FireFox to stop display it, revealing whatever was 
underneath. The only thing it doesn't seem to work on is content embedded by 
3rd party plugins, which for the most part means Flash animations.

https://addons.mozilla.org/firefox/79/

    - Oliver

Oliver Wong wrote:

>     If you're using FireFox, a handy plugin is "nuke anything". It lets you
> right click on almost anything within the FireFox browser (paragraphs,
> floating boxes, images, flash animations, etc.), and choose "Remove this
> object", to cause FireFox to stop display it, revealing whatever was
> underneath.

It is also useful if an object is wider than the browser windows and
text has flowed to that width and requires scrolling.  Nuke the object
and the text becomes readable.

I also use ImageZoom which allows images to be zoomed in size - larger
to reduce eye strain or smaller to adjust text flow without nuking.

> The only thing it doesn't seem to work on is content embedded by
> 3rd party plugins, which for the most part means Flash animations.

Flash Block fixes those.  It doesn't even download the flash unless you
click it.

AniBlock stops those damned animated gif adverts but doesn't have a
version for later Firefox.

- **From:** "Oliver Wong" <owong@castortech.com>
- **Date:** 2006-11-08T10:50:07-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Q0n4h.113406$VK2.1366639@wagner.videotron.net>`
- **References:** `<YtK2h.1898$0r.1534@newsread1.news.pas.earthlink.net> <eifut0$4fn$1@reader2.panix.com> <4r3f9jFpdpc4U1@individual.net> <hehpk2hq7pk0q4arvstum7vhci5rhsvuo1@4ax.com> <4r50ghFpg38pU1@individual.net> <d2muk2l53uqhlbo7c53hj6mrv7s8u1ku6p@4ax.com> <12kuq2q4hrua0b8@news.supernews.com> <vsruk21da5vbef7sdmlpm0vc54atvnhke4@4ax.com> <1162924582.847762.316340@e3g2000cwe.googlegroups.com> <4rcl7mFqq65eU1@mid.individual.net>`

```

"Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote in message 
news:4rcl7mFqq65eU1@mid.individual.net...
>
> Nobody developing a web site wants to limit the accessibility of it, 
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
> goal I am currently trying to reach, but it certainly isn't easy.

    If you do everything on the webserver, you can't implement a map that 
the user can click and drag around, like Google did 
(http://maps.google.com/). At best, the user would click on a "scroll left" 
button, and the entire page would refresh as the new image is downloaded.

    I was really hoping Java would have taken off more than it did. Using 
Java Webstart, a user could click on a weblink, which would *stream* a 
self-contained Java program onto the user's computer. The program is run in 
a sandbox, and so it cannot for example access local files, activate the 
printer or microphone, or connect to any servers except the one it was 
downloaded from, unless it displays a standard confirmation box requesting 
permission for this access from the user.

    So security isn't a problem, but you have the full GUI functionality 
available to you: tables, lists, drop down menus, etc., without resorting to 
HTML+JavaScript tricks. List items can be sorted locally on the client's 
computer, as opposed to sending a request to sort to the webserver, sorting 
it there, and sending the results back to the client. The application being 
"too big" isn't a problem either, because the application is streamed, and 
thus can start running before all the code has been downloaded.

http://java.sun.com/products/javawebstart/demos.html

    Try implementing the drawing program in HTML+JavaScript. It's possible, 
but it'll take a lot more effort than writing it in Java.

    - Oliver
```

- **From:** "Oliver Wong" <owong@castortech.com>
- **Date:** 2006-11-09T14:09:08-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<p1L4h.19189$Xz6.63658@weber.videotron.net>`
- **References:** `<4r3f9jFpdpc4U1@individual.net> <hehpk2hq7pk0q4arvstum7vhci5rhsvuo1@4ax.com> <4r50ghFpg38pU1@individual.net> <d2muk2l53uqhlbo7c53hj6mrv7s8u1ku6p@4ax.com> <12kuq2q4hrua0b8@news.supernews.com> <vsruk21da5vbef7sdmlpm0vc54atvnhke4@4ax.com> <1162924582.847762.316340@e3g2000cwe.googlegroups.com> <4rcl7mFqq65eU1@mid.individual.net> <1163022510.176357.309590@e3g2000cwe.googlegroups.com> <4rfa2mFqk8vvU1@mid.individual.net> <epH4h.13261$Xz6.26387@weber.videotron.net> <mpj6l2t34henug7t6stjs4ncqv5t6ehih7@4ax.com>`

```

"Howard Brazee" <howard@brazee.net> wrote in message 
news:mpj6l2t34henug7t6stjs4ncqv5t6ehih7@4ax.com...
>
> I've never used cell phone browsers - but I imagine they have to be
> pretty simple.    Do web pages have phone optimal designs?

    Someone (perhaps many people got together and) invented WML which is a 
simplified version of HTML designed to be easier to parse and handle. 
http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wireless_Markup_Language The idea was that cell 
phones don't have fast enough processors to do all the error correction that 
"real" web browsers are able to do. A lot of the HTML out there is actually 
very poorly written, with lots of syntax errors, etc., but webbrowsers are 
designed to "guess" what the author intended and silently fix those errors. 
Not so with WML: the syntax is much more strict (it's based on XML), which 
makes the job of cell phone browsers easier.

    (Un)fortunately, cell phone CPUs have improved much faster than 
expected, and both IE and Opera have been ported to cell phones, so you have 
a full powered browser, able to handle all the broken HTML out there. So WML 
is pretty much dead now, and never even got a chance to catch on.

    I think most websites which support phone users just develop two 
seperate sets of pages, using plain HTML. One is designed for normal 
resolution (e.g. 800x600 or higher), and another for much smaller resolution 
devices (e.g. 120x90), and they don't really care whether that particular 
device is a cell phone, PDA, or something else. These websites tend to be 
heavily text based (images are present, but they can't be layed out in 
interesting ways, as they simply take up too much screen real estate at such 
low resolutions), and tend to be single column (as opposed to a two-column 
design with one column for navigation links and another column for main 
content).

    Something cool from Japan: they can print a barcode like image into the 
corner of a poster. Take a picture of the poster using the camera on your 
cellphone, and the phone will recognize the barcode as a link, which you can 
click on to take you to a web page.

http://www.kilian-nakamura.com/blog/data/kiosk2.jpg

    So instead of typing in www.dydo-d1.jp into your cellphone, you can just 
take a picture of the code, and instantly be taken to the relevant website.

    - Oliver
```

- **From:** "Oliver Wong" <owong@castortech.com>
- **Date:** 2006-11-09T10:13:58-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BH4h.13674$Xz6.27267@weber.videotron.net>`
- **References:** `<YtK2h.1898$0r.1534@newsread1.news.pas.earthlink.net> <eifut0$4fn$1@reader2.panix.com> <4r3f9jFpdpc4U1@individual.net> <hehpk2hq7pk0q4arvstum7vhci5rhsvuo1@4ax.com> <4r50ghFpg38pU1@individual.net> <d2muk2l53uqhlbo7c53hj6mrv7s8u1ku6p@4ax.com> <12kuq2q4hrua0b8@news.supernews.com> <vsruk21da5vbef7sdmlpm0vc54atvnhke4@4ax.com> <1162924582.847762.316340@e3g2000cwe.googlegroups.com> <4rcl7mFqq65eU1@mid.individual.net> <1163022510.176357.309590@e3g2000cwe.googlegroups.com> <ctf6l2p2f9hvss2n4tlapnsqh56mpuhrbq@4ax.com>`

```
"Howard Brazee" <howard@brazee.net> wrote in message 
news:ctf6l2p2f9hvss2n4tlapnsqh56mpuhrbq@4ax.com...
>I wonder if a plug-in to a browser would allow color-shifting to help
> color-blind people.    That could be very useful, especially if you
> could program it to know which colors one has troubles with.

    While it's certainly possible, I don't know of any plugin that actually 
does this. One small problem is that you're trying to cram more information 
(e.g. perception of 3 separate red, green and blue channels) into a smaller 
space (e.g. 2 seperate red-green and blue channels, for red-green colour 
blindness), so you're losing some information. Most websites probably use 
few-enough colours that you won't run out of target-colours to map onto, 
though.

    Someone did write a Java-plugin that does the reverse: It takes your 
existing (must-be-written-in-Java) program, and renders it as a colourblind 
person might see it, by merging various channels together (e.g. merging the 
red and green channel to simulate red-green colour blindness). It's for 
designers to test out their UI design, rather than for colour-blind users to 
overcome bad designs.

http://weblogs.java.net/blog/kirillcool/archive/2006/09/how_colorblind.html

    - Oliver
```

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6f3d9$45529261$454920f8$13377@KNOLOGY.NET>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<4rcl7mFqq65eU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<YtK2h.1898$0r.1534@newsread1.news.pas.earthlink.net> <eifut0$4fn$1@reader2.panix.com> <4r3f9jFpdpc4U1@individual.net> <hehpk2hq7pk0q4arvstum7vhci5rhsvuo1@4ax.com> <4r50ghFpg38pU1@individual.net> <d2muk2l53uqhlbo7c53hj6mrv7s8u1ku6p@4ax.com> <12kuq2q4hrua0b8@news.supernews.com> <vsruk21da5vbef7sdmlpm0vc54atvnhke4@4ax.com> <1162924582.847762.316340@e3g2000cwe.googlegroups.com> <4rcl7mFqq65eU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
Pete Dashwood wrote:
> When people develop web sites they put in many hours of thought and effort 
> to designing and building. They will use tools that help that process. Those 
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> compatibility, but this is a very expensive tool.

This is kind of like the old "aren't all mainframes IBM mainframes?" 
belief - tools are designed and work with a de facto standard (in this 
case, Internet Exploder 6), to the exclusion of others.  There is lots 
of stuff in IE6 that isn't "standard", but is functional and can be used 
to make great websites.  However, some of these features rely on 
proprietary technology - which is great for |\/|$, but not for the 
"community at large."  (I'm not faulting you (or anyone else, for that 
matter) - you're using the tool as it was advertised.)

> Nobody developing a web site wants to limit the accessibility of it, either 
> by browser or by any other limiting factor. It is a question of what is 
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> should be no problem.

True - but every technique has trade-offs.  Dynamically serving static 
web pages limits the responsiveness of the page itself, and requires 
another round-trip to the server to update items.  There are 
technologies that can assist with this, but any technology that can be 
used can be mis-used.

One of the projects I have is a help file with information about our 
database.  I came up with a process where I have a database about the 
database - all the fields, how they're defined, the definition, what 
standard XML tag is used in interfaces, etc.  I then export this 
information to XML files, which display using an XSL stylesheet. 
Compiled it all into a .chm file (Windows HTML Help), and it worked great!

After a while, I started getting calls and e-mails - hey, how come the 
help file doesn't work?  Turns out that the way IE (the back-end for the 
.chm file output) did that is a way that the Air Force has decided is a 
grave security risk.  Put the file on your personal hard drive, no 
problem.  Hit it from a network share, it doesn't work.  So, even my 
cutting-edge "standard" technology stuff isn't immune from being 
thwarted by security settings.

Not to say we should just throw our hands up and say "screw it" - but 
any solution is going to have folks who can't utilize it.

> You could easily conclude that the best solution is probably to do 
> EVERYTHING on the web server, then simply serve up a dynamically constructed 
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> the experience I have accumulated previously to try and attain this goal.

It's possible.  JavaScript may be disabled by some folks - but it's been 
my experience that it's the easiest way to go as far as DHTML goes.  Of 
course, there's the issue of document.layers vs. document.all - but I've 
found a great cross-compatible way to do it is to use 
document.getElementById or document.getElementsByName to retrieve objects.

Of course, if you don't need client-dynamic pages, you don't really need 
JavaScript.  :)

> It isn't just about browsers, either. There is the question of what the 
> Hosting ISP will allow... can I run COBOL CGI code? Does he support ASP, 
> Java/VB Script on the server? Can I use MySQL or must it be SQL Server?

And what version?  I wrote a site against MySQL 5, only to find out that 
my ISP had 4, and wasn't even going to upgrade to 4.1.  They did move my 
site to another box that had 4.1, but at the time they had no plans to 
go with 5.  The coolest query in the whole system, a single request that 
returned gaps in a sequence, did not work.  :(

> There is much more to it than the average person realises when they just 
> find that their browser doesn't render a certain page correctly.
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> the 85%...

There are simple things that can be done, though, to make sites more 
friendly to the greatest number of browsers and people.  Do a search on 
"<strong> vs. <b>" and look at some of those discussions.  Other search 
topics that provide interesting reading are "semantic HTML" and 
"semantic markup".  Basically, there are existing tags that are more 
descriptive than others for non-visual users, yet are rendered the same 
for regular users.

> "For he that hath, to him shall be given: and he that hath not, from him 
> shall be taken away even that which he hath."

Right - but the context there was the parable of the talents, where two 
servants doubled their master's money, and the third hid it because he 
was afraid.  The moral?  Use that which you have been given, or it will 
be taken away and given to one who will use it.  :)

(Oh yeah - I'm back, and my laptop's fixed...  But, you probably figured 
that out by now.  ;>  )
```

```

LX-i wrote:

> to.  :(  I have a newfound hatred of ad servers...

Firefox + adblock =   ;-)

> As kind of a side tangent - under IE, you can attach whatever code you
> want to a <button> element.  There is no default associated action for
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> but if anyone in here knows of one, I'm all ears.

onclick=javascript action

working example:

<input onclick='popUpCalendar(this, document.selempe.day,
"yyyy-mm-dd")' value="calendar"  type="button">

> > You might use it to drive facilities on the page that have nothing to do
> > with dynamic content.
>
> Why sort of stuff would JavaScript do that isn't dynamic?

The term "Dynamic pages" usually refers to pages that are created
during page load while static pages are just fixed files on the server.

Javascript can be used to create page content at the client side (or
indeed at the server side in some cases) or it can be used on static or
dynamic pages to do stuff like, for example, checking form input, which
isn't dynamic content.
```

pay carriers for moving mail around Europe and Asia.  We had to log them 
there as well for accountability, and for a backup in case the wonderful 
automated system we created them in went down (as it did several times). 
  So, if we started with control number 2300, for example, and at the 
end of our shift, the next control number was 2316, we should have 16 of 
these forms logged.

Using the form I designed, it took maybe 20 seconds per form - I could 
do it sub-10, but I knew how to do it without taking my hands off the 
keyboard.  I trained other folks how to do that, and we had no problems. 
  :)  The other folks were more interested in not doing it than learning 
how to do it quickly - their loss.

```

"LX-i" <lxi0007@netscape.net> wrote in message 
news:1bca5$4553e146$454920f8$32651@KNOLOGY.NET...
>
> As kind of a side tangent - under IE, you can attach whatever code you 
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> knows of one, I'm all ears.

http://www.w3.org/TR/html4/interact/forms.html#h-17.5

    I haven't used the button tag myself, but according to the World Wide 
Web Consortium, a button is supposed to act like a <input type="submit"/> if 
no type is specified (so it looks like IE's behaviour is non-standard in 
this respect). If you want the "do-nothing" behaviour, you have to specify 
the type as being "button". e.g.:

<button type="button">Click me</button>

    - Oliver
```

```
On Wed, 08 Nov 2006 20:29:09 -0600, LX-i <lxi0007@netscape.net> wrote:

>This is kind of like the old "aren't all mainframes IBM mainframes?" 
>belief - tools are designed and work with a de facto standard (in this 
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>matter) - you're using the tool as it was advertised.)

We've discovered another problem with those powerful nifty tools.

Because of their power, malware uses them as well, resulting in
browsers that give users the ability to turn them off.   There is a
reason Firefox and Opera don't enable Active-X.

So if your web site utilizes this new powerful feature - don't be
surprised if customers can't access it next month.
```

>Doc, I'm interested in your backup strategy.  I have a laptop with XP
>on it and I have a large external HD as well and have been looking for
>something that I can easily back up my entire laptop drive to.  Are
>saying Acronis can do this (XP - External HD)?

My experience is that Acronis will do *exactly* that... working with a 
Dell Latitude 505 running WinXP I have been called when the machine was 
'doing weird stuff'.  I ran a chkdsk /f, managed to reboot and install 
Acronis, run a full backup to an external USB drive, replace the fried 
disk in the laptop and do a bare-metal restore by booting off the CD.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: OT: windoze woes and full rant mode is on

- **Date:** 2006-11-05T01:40:15+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4r3g1kFpg4heU1@individual.net>`
- **References:** `<YtK2h.1898$0r.1534@newsread1.news.pas.earthlink.net> <iradnXHLMMi1FtbYnZ2dnUVZ_u6dnZ2d@giganews.com> <vpN2h.21536$TV3.7298@newssvr21.news.prodigy.com>`

```

"Michael Mattias" <mmattias@talsystems.com> wrote in message 
news:vpN2h.21536$TV3.7298@newssvr21.news.prodigy.com...
>>> I hate the MSN Messenger icon in my system tray...
>
> I opened it, hit options, an unchecked "Start Windows Messenger when 
> Windows starts."
>

For Office 2003  with Windows XP Pro...

1. Open it. (Can do this from the icon on the toolbar by double clicking).
2. Options>Preferences
3. Uncheck "Run Windows Messenger when Windows starts."

It will be gone when you reboot.

Pete.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: OT: windoze woes and full rant mode is on

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** Robin Lee <robinlee@news.com>
- **Date:** 2006-11-04T16:39:27-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3rudncKD4NRYldDYnZ2dnUVZ_ridnZ2d@giganews.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<4r3g1kFpg4heU1@individual.net>`
- **References:** `<YtK2h.1898$0r.1534@newsread1.news.pas.earthlink.net> <iradnXHLMMi1FtbYnZ2dnUVZ_u6dnZ2d@giganews.com> <vpN2h.21536$TV3.7298@newssvr21.news.prodigy.com> <4r3g1kFpg4heU1@individual.net>`

```
Pete Dashwood wrote:
> "Michael Mattias" <mmattias@talsystems.com> wrote in message 
> news:vpN2h.21536$TV3.7298@newssvr21.news.prodigy.com...
…[15 more quoted lines elided]…
>  

We seem to be discussing two *different* functions here.  The action you've 
described should stop Windows Messenger from starting when Windows starts.

The problem which plagued me (and presumably the originator of this thread) 
is the "feature" whereby Office Outlook has the power to autonomously invoke 
the MSN Messenger and place it in the system tray, long after the last time 
Windows was restarted - hours, days, or even weeks later. This is the issue 
which was addressed by the PC Magazine hack and referenced in the original post.

Elsewhere in the thread it was asked if this Messenger was written in COBOL 
and if not then this discussion belongs in a different newsgroup.  While I 
agree in principal, please let me make two points here.  First, if it were 
written in COBOL it would be an entirely different program... not as a 
result of the nature of the language, but the nature of the programmer. It 
would only execute when requested, would consume few resources, do the task 
for which it was intended and courteously remove itself from memory once the 
task is completed.

Secondly, I am probably not the first person to ever come to the realization 
that working with a computer presents us with two tasks: one is to make the 
computer do what we wish, and the other (far more difficult) task is to keep 
it from doing thinks which we do not wish it to do.

It *appears* that the purpose of this MSN feature is that someone can send 
an email which can then fire up a chat client on the remote end ... an 
invitation to join the collective as it were.  I don't know why Microsoft 
would include such a "feature".  Remember this is the company that gave us 
the web browser that can format your hard drive. Presumably some programmer 
thought it would be cool.

Resistance is futile.
```

- **References:** `<YtK2h.1898$0r.1534@newsread1.news.pas.earthlink.net> <iradnXHLMMi1FtbYnZ2dnUVZ_u6dnZ2d@giganews.com> <vpN2h.21536$TV3.7298@newssvr21.news.prodigy.com> <4r3g1kFpg4heU1@individual.net> <3rudncKD4NRYldDYnZ2dnUVZ_ridnZ2d@giganews.com> <4r5183FprsivU1@individual.net> <_emdnfr8Kuq7wdDYnZ2dnUVZ_v6dnZ2d@giganews.com> <4r73apFq7lstU1@individual.net> <_WP3h.174481$R52.84564@fe07.news.easynews.com>`

```
William M. Klein wrote:
> 
>>> If your Outlook 2003 is still starting the MSN Messenger, then uncheck the 
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> 

Select "Tools" from the top bar, then "Options" from the drop-down list 
(you're almost there).  This presents a property sheet with six tabs across 
the top (from left to right): Preferences, Mail Setup, Mail Format, 
Spelling, Security, and "Other" is the last tab to the right on top.

The check box at the bottom of this last sheet is the "Person names smart 
tag" option which evidently allows an email to initiate MSN Messenger.

It seems like they tried to hide this in the farthest, most remote corner of 
the system.

Good luck,
-R
```

## Thread: problem w/READ INTO in COBOL/VSE? — 16 msgs

### problem w/READ INTO in COBOL/VSE?

- **From:** "Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com>
- **Date:** 2006-11-03T10:52:55-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4r1dvnFoseo5U1@individual.net>`

```
The following was posted by Michael Rosinger on the vse-l listserv.  Any
thoughts?

>>> Michael Rosinger<mrosinger@cciws.com> 11/03/06 7:27 AM >>>
List,

I am writing a simple COBOL/VSE program where I am reading a SD file and 
processing it. I am using the READ INTO option. According to the manual (and

all my years of experience) the BOTH the record area AND the target of the 
INTO clause are supposed to be populated with the contents of the record (as

long as the READ was successful).

Well, it's not working that way. I added DISPLAYs of both areas immediately

after the READ and the W-S area (target of INTO) is populated but the file 
area for the record is not!

I've conferred with the manual and I am playing by the rules. Has anyone 
else encountered this? Or am I losing it?

We are VSE/ESA 2.7.3 with COBOL/VSE 1.1.1.  TIA!
```

#### ↳ Re: problem w/READ INTO in COBOL/VSE?

- **From:** Howard Brazee <howard@brazee.net>

On Fri, 3 Nov 2006 10:52:55 -0700, "Frank Swarbrick"
<Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote:

>I am writing a simple COBOL/VSE program where I am reading a SD file and 
>processing it. I am using the READ INTO option. According to the manual (and
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>long as the READ was successful).

How are you reading an SD file?    Those are sort files, 

  SORT SORT-FILE                    
      ON ASCENDING KEY SORT-KEY     
      USING PRINT-FILE   

and/or           
      GIVING PRINT-FILE            

and/or
   INPUT PROCEDURE 2000-SORT-INPUT     
  OUTPUT PROCEDURE 5000-SORT-OUTPUT
```

Sorry, SD in this case refers to a VSE "sequential disk" file.

The code was not posted, but here's my guess at what it looks like (only
relevant code posted):

SELECT MYFILE ASSIGN TO MYFIL.

FD  MYFILE.
01  MYREC PIC X(80).

WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
01  WS-MYREC PIC X(80).

READ MYFILE INTO WS-MYREC
IF MYREC = WS-MYREC
    DISPLAY 'EXPECTED'
ELSE
    DISPLAY 'UNEXPECTED'
END-IF.

Being lazy I have not tried it myself to see if I get the same results as
the OP...

Frank

(To vse-l people, I cross-posted Mike's original message to comp.lang.cobol
to see if anyone could shed some light on how this *should* work.)

As I posted in the initial message, this is not my issue.  I was simply
forwarding on an issue as posted by someone else.

In any case, here is a little test program that demonstrates the problem:

000001 IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.                  
000002 PROGRAM-ID.    READINTO.                  
000003 ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.                     
000004 INPUT-OUTPUT SECTION.                     
000005 FILE-CONTROL.                             
000006     SELECT TEST-FILE                      
000007         ASSIGN TO TFIL.                   
000008                                           
000009 DATA DIVISION.                            
000010 FILE SECTION.                             
000011 FD  TEST-FILE                             
000012     RECORDING MODE F.                     
000013 01  TEST-RECORD                 PIC X(80).
000014                                           
000015 WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.                  
000016 01  WS-RECORD                   PIC X(80).
000017                                           
000018 PROCEDURE DIVISION.                       
000019     OPEN INPUT TEST-FILE                  
000020     READ TEST-FILE INTO TEST-RECORD       
000021     DISPLAY TEST-RECORD                   
000022     DISPLAY WS-RECORD                     
000023     IF TEST-RECORD = WS-RECORD            
000024         DISPLAY 'EXPECTED'                       
000025     ELSE                                         
000026         DISPLAY 'UNEXPECTED'                     
000027     END-IF                                       
000028     CLOSE TEST-FILE                              
000029                                                  
000030     OPEN INPUT TEST-FILE                         
000031     READ TEST-FILE                               
000032     MOVE TEST-RECORD TO WS-RECORD                
000033     DISPLAY TEST-RECORD                          
000034     DISPLAY WS-RECORD                            
000035     IF TEST-RECORD = WS-RECORD                   
000036         DISPLAY 'EXPECTED'                       
000037     ELSE                                         
000038         DISPLAY 'UNEXPECTED'                     
000039     END-IF                                       
000040     CLOSE TEST-FILE                              
000041     GOBACK.                                      
000042                                                  
000043 END PROGRAM READINTO.                            

Unless I'm mistaken, the original poster expects that TEST-RECORD and
WS-RECORD will be the same after both types of reads (well, the second after
the READ / MOVE set).  What I am getting as a result is the following:
THIS IS AN 80 CHARACTER LINE, TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST
TEST.
                                                                            
   
UNEXPECTED                                                                  
   
THIS IS AN 80 CHARACTER LINE, TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST
TEST.
THIS IS AN 80 CHARACTER LINE, TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST TEST
TEST.
EXPECTED                                                                    
   

The "blank" line is actually 80 bytes of "low-values".

All I know is it is not 'working as expected'.  Whether or not it is
actually working correctly, just not as expected, I have no idea.

This is, by the way, COBOL for VSE/ESA 1.1.1.  Also, an 'SD' file is a SAM
file.  It is not a VSAM ESDS.

Frank

EUREKA !!! (unless you made a typo).  The first section has

     READ TEST-FILE INTO TEST-RECORD

instead of

    READ TEST-FILE INTO WS-RECORD

Trying to do a "read into" the record-area is a DEFINITE "no-no" !!!
```

```

Frank Swarbrick wrote:
> Sorry, SD in this case refers to a VSE "sequential disk" file.
>
> The code was not posted, but here's my guess at what it looks like (only
> relevant code posted):

Guesses may not be enough. I can think of many reasons why they won't
match.

> SELECT MYFILE ASSIGN TO MYFIL.
>
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> READ MYFILE INTO WS-MYREC

An AT END may be useful as if the read fails the move to WS won't be
done.

> IF MYREC = WS-MYREC
>     DISPLAY 'EXPECTED'
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> the OP...

Another possibility is if the file has variable records then the READ
will only overwrite the FD area up to the size of the record but the
implict MOVE will move that record size and then clear the remainder of
the WS record area.  ie. after the size that the actual recod is the FD
area will be junk and the WS area will be spaces.
```

#### ↳ Re: problem w/READ INTO in COBOL/VSE?

- **From:** "Alistair" <alistair@ld50macca.demon.co.uk>
- **Date:** 2006-11-03T11:55:13-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1162583712.977012.277610@m73g2000cwd.googlegroups.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<4r1dvnFoseo5U1@individual.net>`
- **References:** `<4r1dvnFoseo5U1@individual.net>`

```

Frank Swarbrick wrote:
> The following was posted by Michael Rosinger on the vse-l listserv.  Any
> thoughts?
…[16 more quoted lines elided]…
>

The FD in the Cobol deck will translate to a GET command addressing a
specified record area (the one defined in working storage by the
plaintiff) into which the program places the record (according to the
DCB used). The record area within the datablock will not be available
to the program. Hence, you can view the working storage record but not
the whole of the block of data.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: problem w/READ INTO in COBOL/VSE?

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2006-11-03T21:20:12+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<foO2h.565992$Pi2.16265@fe08.news.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<4r1dvnFoseo5U1@individual.net> <1162583712.977012.277610@m73g2000cwd.googlegroups.com>`

```
Alistair,
    I *think* that what you are saying isn't quite right.  As far as I know all 
IBM COBOL's do whatever it takes to get the code to work in a 
"standard-conforming" manner which means that the record area SHOULD contain the 
same data as the WS area.  The only exception to this (that I can think of) is 
something like:

FD  File1.
01   Alpha1 Pic XXXXX.

  ..WS

01  AlphaEd-1   Pic XX/XXBX.
  ...
Read File1 into AlphaEd-1.

In that case, I think the WS version will contain an "edited" version of the FD 
data.  I don't think this is exactly what Frank was talking about, but if so, 
then the two data areas will NOT match.
```

> something like:

How about if the WS area is shorter than the file record.  That will
work and will silently truncate the data causing it to be different.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: problem w/READ INTO in COBOL/VSE?

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2006-11-06T23:50:32+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<cTP3h.606492$Pi2.480258@fe08.news.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<4r1dvnFoseo5U1@individual.net> <1162583712.977012.277610@m73g2000cwd.googlegroups.com> <foO2h.565992$Pi2.16265@fe08.news.easynews.com> <1162837505.514240.120900@i42g2000cwa.googlegroups.com>`

```
To be perfectly accurate, the WS item will contain the same data "as if" the 
"record area" (01 under the FD) was move to it.  (Editing, padding, truncation, 
etc) will occur.

Sorry I wasn't clearer earlier.

NOTE:
  If there are 2 or more 01-levels under the FD with different sizes, only the 
"correct length" of the record area will be defined.
```

<a id="t-c04d863758"></a>
## Thread: OT: Job References; are they any real value? — 6 msgs

_Topics: [`Jobs, careers, recruiting, salary`](topics.md#jobs) · [`Tutorials, books, learning`](topics.md#learning) · [`Off-topic and spam`](topics.md#spam)_

### OT: Job References; are they any real value?

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2006-11-04T14:36:51+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4r295lFp6h0oU1@individual.net>`

```
A poster to another thread expressed concern that, if he was fired from his 
present job, he would have great difficulty getting re-employed, as the new 
employer would take up a reference and find he had been dismissed.

This made me think about the whole question of references. I'd be interested 
to hear the views of other forum members, from both sides (employer and 
prospective employee), as to how much weight is actually attached to these 
and how much should be...

Here are my thoughts on it... (comments, disagreements, agreement, all 
welcomed...)

For the EMPLOYER:

1.  Nobody is going to show you a reference that says they suck.
2.  Nobody is going to refer you to someone who is likely to say bad things 
about them.
3.  The very worst people will get their friends at the old job to write 
them a reference (or will do it themselves...)

Given the above, how much credibility can a reference actually carry?  Even 
with genuine good ones, there is no guarantee that the prospect will fit 
into your environment as well as they did at the previous place. Every 
workplace environment is different; every 'corporate culture' is different, 
and these factors can greatly affect performance on the shop floor.

Even assuming you believe the reference and employ the prospect, what good 
does the reference do if they turn out to be different in your 
environment...?

"Er... Mr. Jones, IT manager? You remember you gave a reference on Peter 
Punchcard who was one of your employees a while back? You said 'he is an 
ideal employee, calm under stress and produces work of high quality.'"?

"Yes, I remember Peter. He was solid and reliable."

"Well, he wrote some code that was severely criticised in the review 
walkthrough. He didn't take it well."

"I'm surprised at that."

"He stormed out of the meeting, went to his desk,  pulled out a gun and shot 
three co-workers dead. He then defiled the Lead Business Analyst with a 
rolled up program listing, urinated in the corner cubicle (while it was 
occupied), and is currently holding the operations manager hostage. You can 
possibly hear the sirens in the background; we are waiting for the SWAT team 
to arrive."

"Well, that's terrible! But why are you phoning me?"

"I intend to sue you for punitive damages, given that you were completely 
wrong in your reference."

"Ha! I don't think so...That reference carries no legal weight or 
responsibility whatsoever, it is an opinion not a fact, and has no value of 
any kind in or out of a Court of Law. I stated my opinion on how Peter 
behaved when he worked for us; I made no guarantee as to his future 
behaviour. Sue away if you want... you'll end up incurring legal costs on 
top of your current problems." Click! The phone goes dead...

If you are an ex-employer and someone phones you for a reference on one of 
your ex-employees, be VERY careful what you say... see the next point, 
below.

On the occasions when I am required to recruit people, I NEVER ask for or 
require references. If they have them and offer them, I will do the polite 
thing and look at them, but they cut absolutely no ice with me.

I have employed people who were supposed to be "unemployable" (according to 
previous managers they had, and who were shocked to hear I had taken them 
on), and some of them (not all :-)) were the best people I ever worked with. 
Human Beings are very complex creatures; we respond completely differently 
in different environments.



For the EMPLOYEE:

1. A future employer is (probably... - more enlightened companies are 
dropping this practice and relying on their own assessments... and, in some 
cases, tests...) going to ask for a reference. Given that you're leaving 
because you are pissed off with where you work, what can you do about a 
reference? The company is legally (in all the jurisdictions where I have 
worked) required to provide a 'Certificate of Service'. This states the 
dates you were employed from and to. They are NOT required to make any 
comment as to your suitability or otherwise. If they do and it is bad, you 
may have a case for libel.  If you refer someone to them for a telephone 
reference and they say bad things about you, you may have a case for 
slander. Makes the whole reference thing pretty pointless, doesn't it?

2. If your new prospective employer is pretty serious about having a 
reference (usually they are driven by SOP which was formulated in some ivory 
tower in Xanadu by Human Resources people who have no idea what life in the 
trenches is like), you will need to get SOMEONE to say nice things about 
you. If your manager isn't likely to, (and more often than not, he's the 
reason you are moving on...) you will need to get a colleague or a drinking 
buddy and invent a title for them like "Team Leader" or "Senior DB 
Administrator".  If you feel that this is verging on the shady, remember 
that the whole process is pointless anyway, and it is just like ticking 
boxes on a Tick IT form, or writing 8 hours on a timesheet  (you did turn up 
for work today, right?), or charging the time you spent learning how to 
write JCL and play online Backgammon, against the Testing budget for the new 
application that you were employed to help develop... :-)

Very occasionally, you will be moving on regretfully, due to exterior 
factors. Take this opportunity to get a genuine and glowing reference from 
your Boss. (You can intersperse a few of these amongst the ones from point 2 
and it gives the whole collection a bit more credibility...)

In GENERAL:

I have had some amazing references. "His personal work is of the standard 
one would expect from one whose job it is to improve the work of others." 
(loved that, treasured it for years. Written by a mentor (sadly, now 
deceased)when I was a young programmer... ), "His unfailing enthusiasm and 
capability is an inspiration to the people who work with him."   (I never 
knew it until they told me... :-))... the point is, that no matter how many 
you have, and no matter how glowing they may be, ...they are worthless.

The only ones that MAY have some value are telephone ones, where you have no 
idea what they are likely to say about you, and you have very little 
comeback if they denigrate you.

For the last contract I did in Auckland the company took the most extensive 
references of anyone I have ever worked with. They wanted males and females 
who had worked for me and for whom I had worked. It was all telephone and 
involved 8 referrees on 4 continents. I passed, even though I had no idea 
WHAT the people might say and had never asked any of them to be referees 
before. Did I do the job any better because of this? No. Did this provide 
any more real credibility for me than my actually doing the job? No. Did it 
provide my prospective employer with any kind of guarantee as to my worth? 
No.

Pointless. It is simply an HR time waste.

DISCLAIMER:

For the last 30 years I have worked only as a free lance and on a contract 
basis. Normally, with contractors, companies don't seem to require 
references.

I think the theory is that if they take you on and you obviously can't do 
the job, they can fire you PDQ and get someone else; it ain't so easy with a 
permanent employee.

The Auckland company mentioned above was a notable exception. Maybe it's a 
Kiwi thing, I haven't worked here for a very long time and NZ does tend to 
be pretty conservative.


BOTTOM LINE:

Job references are a pointless waste of everybody's time. Prospective 
applicants should be employed on their merit, based on what they showed in 
an interview. Prospective employers should hone their interview skills and 
back their own judgement.

Pete.
```

#### ↳ Re: Job References; are they any real value?

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <mmattias@talsystems.com>
- **Date:** 2006-11-04T15:07:41+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1123h.21696$TV3.6509@newssvr21.news.prodigy.com>`
- **References:** `<4r295lFp6h0oU1@individual.net>`

```
You brought up the litigation thing... which results in the functional 
equivalent of your "certificate of service".. about all you can get from any 
company here (USA) with an in-house counsel are dates of service and 
official job title. (Maybe it's not our foreign policy which upsets so many 
around the world, it's our surfeit of lawyers with nothing better to do than 
file tort claims?)

I'm a lot like you, though: I've been a contractor/consultant for fifteen 
years and references requested are usually limited to "capabilities" and any 
question about 'fitting in' as a full-time employee are moot.

Then again, just being able to provide a nice list with names and phone 
numbers I think has its own intrinsic value as sales literature. And if the 
prospect actually checks? Fine by me. I've invested in lot in creating that 
list, and it's about time to earn a fair return on that investment.

When I was an employer, I was able to actually check references (this was 
before litigation was a way of life). As you say, people were generally 
reluctant to say anything negative so the 'downside' evaluation was more 
difficult than the 'upside' evaluation. But when conducting interviews, I 
always felt I could get a pretty good idea of what really happened at a 
previous employer simply by observing body language when I asked, "So why 
did you leave that position?" (You can safely infer a lot from a squirm).

-
Michael C. Mattias
Tal Systems Inc.
Racine WI
mmattias@talsystems.com
```

Well I have to weigh in on the side of "References have limited value".

No one dares give a bad reference here in the USA for fear of a
lawsuit.

When hiring I prefer to hire someone I know or is known by someone I
know well.

If I don't have either, then I carefully monitor the new-hire's work
and terminate quickly if a problem surfaces. One of my college
professors once said "If an employee needs terminated after the
probationary period, it is usually management's fault for not doing
their job".

Fortunately in our business we can tell very quickly if a new-hire has
the right-stuff.

#### ↳ Re: OT: Job References; are they any real value?

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2006-11-06T13:07:21+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<einc29$6m2$1@reader2.panix.com>`

```
In article <4r295lFp6h0oU1@individual.net>,
Pete Dashwood <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:

[snip]

>This made me think about the whole question of references. I'd be interested 
>to hear the views of other forum members, from both sides (employer and 
>prospective employee), as to how much weight is actually attached to these 
>and how much should be...

I haven't been an employee (except as a legal fiction for a temp agency, 
stuff that has to do with intricacies of tax laws in the USA) for decades 
now; the job-hunting drill, for me, usually consists of:

1) I come down off a contract and send off updated brag-sheets to various 
head-hunters, some that I've worked with in the past and are still in 
business (body-shops can be rather... transient) and others which are 
freshly-sprung from the ground, like mushrooms after a storm.

2) Folks at either sort of place, new or old, will sometimes ask me for 
references.  I ask if they have an actual slot in mind or if they're just 
filling in check-boxes... I don't like my references to be bothered with a 
pimp's 'look, I'm busy!' activities.  If there's a live one on the line I 
give names and numbers of folks I've worked with.

3) Sometimes they call the numbers and find someone I've worked with... 
and sometimes not, folks in this business can be a bit transient, as well.

4) The people they manage to reach give glowing evaluations of my 
capabilities and skills... something along the lines of 'Wonderful 
programmer... great programmer... singing programmer'.

5) The bodyshopper is either satisfied with these reports or dissatisfied 
('Singing programmer?  Too bad... the client is looking for a singing *and 
dancing* programmer.')

6) The person who supplied the reference gives me a call, lets me know 
that folks are looking into my background and tells me that I should send 
off the usual payment... oh, all right, the last part I made up.

7) The bodyshopper calls the client and says 'Got a good one here, 
relevant experience, good refs... let's set up an interview.'  The 
client-contacts responds with something along the lines of 
'zzzzZZZZzzzz... huh? whuh? oh, OK, send him in/let's set up a phone 
tech/sorry, the slot's been filled/hey, we were running a blind ad to 
determine rates.'

... and day passes into night, summer into autumn, the planets dance 
through their epicycles and 'twas e'er thus.

DD
```

## Thread: VSAM Error Code 04 — 9 msgs

_Topics: [`VSAM, files, sorting`](topics.md#files)_

### VSAM Error Code 04

- **From:** SkippyPB <swiegand@neo.rr.NOSPAM.com>
- **Date:** 2006-11-07T15:54:19-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<urr1l2psaknq4umoae6dqgg88tkqv0b599@4ax.com>`

```
This is embarrasing.  I've been a Cobol programmer for nearly 30
years.  I've done Systems work, CICS work, VM work and coded on IBM
mainframes op systems from DOS through z/OS.  But for the life of me,
I cannot figure out what is wrong with what is essentially a simple
program.  Hopefully, someone here will say, "You dummy!  You forgot
to..." whatever.

Here are the specifics:

I have the following Select Statement:

SELECT MASTER01-IN
    ASSIGN TO MAST01I
   ORGANIZATION IS INDEXED
    ACCESS MODE IS SEQUENTIAL
    FILE STATUS IS WS-FILE-STATUS
    RECORD KEY IS MAST01-KEY.

Then we have the following FD:

FD  MASTER01-IN.
01  MASTER01-RECORD.
     03  MAST01-KEY           PIC  X(19).
     03  FILLER                     PIC (2481).

Pretty simple, yes?  The file is opened with no errors.  A simple read
is done:

READ MASTER01-IN.

WS-FILE-STATUS is checked and we find that it contains 04.  The entire
return code is 0004.  This says that there is a conflict between the
record length and fixed file attributes.

However, a LISTCAT shows the file is not fixed.  It has a MAXIMUM
record length of 2500 and an Average record length of 1440.  The first
record on file (according to a File Aid dump) says the length is 1600
and something long, well within the allocated 2500 bytes.

Just for kicks, I added 4 bytes to the record length and tried again.
This time I got a 0039 error code - file attributes conflict of actual
vs. specified.

The file is used in online without any problems.  I'm trying to access
it in a batch Cobol program.  What have I missed?  What have I done
wrong?  Someone PLEASE give me a clue.

Thanks.



          ////
         (o o)
-oOO--(_)--OOo-


"I was such an ugly baby...My mother never breast fed me.
She told me that she only liked me as a friend..."
-- RODNEY DANGERFIELD
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~

Remove nospam to email me.

Steve
```

#### ↳ Re: VSAM Error Code 04

- **From:** Clark F Morris <cfmpublic@ns.sympatico.ca>
- **Date:** 2006-11-07T21:08:21+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7bt1l21gi03mhrsrckg0ti5hi0nhl1nl0i@4ax.com>`

>years.  I've done Systems work, CICS work, VM work and coded on IBM

#### ↳ Re: VSAM Error Code 04

- **From:** "Richard" <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2006-11-07T14:04:37-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1162937077.389984.306310@b28g2000cwb.googlegroups.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<urr1l2psaknq4umoae6dqgg88tkqv0b599@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<urr1l2psaknq4umoae6dqgg88tkqv0b599@4ax.com>`

```

SkippyPB wrote:

> WS-FILE-STATUS is checked and we find that it contains 04.  The entire
> return code is 0004.  This says that there is a conflict between the
> record length and fixed file attributes.

When testing File Status for success it is necessary to only test the
first byte for being zero. This indicates successful completion (in
this case a read). The second byte may contain additional information
in which case a test for '00' incorrectly shows that it 'failed' even
though the operation was successful.

The problem seems to be that you have no mechanism by which the system
can tell you the length of the actual record read.  As the record area
is only changed to the point of the end of the record then junk will
remain beyond that point, but you are not being told where that point
is because there is no indicator to hold the length.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: VSAM Error Code 04

- **From:** Howard Brazee <howard@brazee.net>
- **Date:** 2006-11-08T07:28:04-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<p8q3l29368ev95vs03rok1s912345h5lbo@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<urr1l2psaknq4umoae6dqgg88tkqv0b599@4ax.com> <1162937077.389984.306310@b28g2000cwb.googlegroups.com>`

```
On 7 Nov 2006 14:04:37 -0800, "Richard" <riplin@Azonic.co.nz> wrote:

>When testing File Status for success it is necessary to only test the
>first byte for being zero. This indicates successful completion (in
>this case a read). The second byte may contain additional information
>in which case a test for '00' incorrectly shows that it 'failed' even
>though the operation was successful.

Although "97" also indicates successful open on IBM mainframes.
```

- **From:** "Richard" <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1162937326.668093.205630@m73g2000cwd.googlegroups.com>`

It is 'fixed (file attributes)' not '(fixed file) attributes'.  That
is: the fixed attributes of the file.
